Discussion Name: Was Donald Trump a Good President?

1. Donald Trump was a good president.
1.1. Pro: The success of President Trump's policies meant that he was one of the best presidents.
1.1.1. Pro: President Trump reformed all aspects of the US's immigration system, reducing both legal and illegal immigration.
1.1.1.1. Pro: Illegal immigration, which is a [huge drain](https://cis.org/Report/Costs-Immigration)(- County of Los Angeles, Chief Administrative Officer. Report on the Fiscal Costs of Illegal Aliens in Los Angeles County. 1991.\n\nThis report assessed taxes paid to the county by an estimated 770,000 illegal aliens and their service and assistance costs to the county. It found county revenues of $137.6 million and county outlays of $413.8 million, for a deficit for illegals of $276.2 million in FY'91.\n\n- State of Texas, Governor's Office of Immigration and Refugee Affairs \(GOIRA\). Estimates of the Undocumented Population. 1993.\n\nGOIRA estimated there were 550,000 illegal aliens in Texas in 1992. They paid $290 million in state and local taxes and generated state and local service and assistance costs of $456 million, for a deficit of $166 million. Applying the lower estimate of the Immigration and Naturalization Service \(INS\) of 350,000 illegal aliens in Texas, GOlRA estimated total costs and revenues at $313 million and $183 million respectively, for a deficit of $130 million.) on the United State's welfare state, was addressed by the Trump administration.
1.1.1.1.1. Pro: President Trump planned to [introduce](https://time.com/5590730/trump-immigration-plan-congress/)(Drafted by top advisers Jared Kushner and Stephen Miller, the proposal outlines an immigration system that focuses mostly on those with specific professional skills and education, replacing decades-old laws favoring relatives of other immigrants.\n\n“It would be a big departure from our current system,” says Stephen Yale-Loehr, a professor of immigration law practice at Cornell University. “Right now two-thirds of all immigrants who are admitted are based on some kind of family characteristic.”) a new merit-based system for legal immigration to the United States, where those who could positively contribute to the economy would be given visas.
1.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: President Trump called for an overhaul of the immigration system to make it [merit-based](https://www.us-immigration.com/blog/trumps-raise-act-proposes-merit-based-immigration-system/)(What is a merit-based green card system?\n\nA merit-based green card system uses a point system to determine who can immigrate to and live in a country. Many countries award points based on job, career or language skills. Most merit-based systems focus on strengthening the host country’s economy.\n\nAlong that line, in February of 2017, U.S. Senators Tom Cotton and David Perdue introduced the RAISE Act, Senate Bill 354. RAISE is an acronym that stands for Reforming American Immigration for Strong Employment. It is part of a larger plan to make the U.S. immigration system more merit-based.) rather than lottery-based.
1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: The primary effect of this policy will be more competition for well-paying jobs, likely with lower wages as a result.
1.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: There will be many effects, and the above claim is a gross simplification. The policy will bring much-needed skills into the country which will boost wealth for everyone in the long run. It will also increase wages for low skilled jobs as employers will be less able to rely on illegal immigrants who are willing to work for less money for a variety of reasons.
1.1.1.1.1.1.2. Con: As a candidate who is unreliable and [often](https://www.politifact.com/personalities/donald-trump/) [lies](https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2018/09/12/anatomy-trump-rally-percent-claims-are-false-misleading-or-lacking-evidence/?utm_term=.3cb2328191c5), the fact the policies he's gone forward with on immigration tell much more than the policies he says he intends to go forward with.
1.1.1.1.1.1.3. Con: Conversely, President Trump has also called for [reducing](http://fortune.com/2017/01/14/congress-h1b-immigration/) the number of H1-B visas - highly qualified people who should have a lot of merit.
1.1.1.1.2. Con: Immigrants provide great economic benefit and have a negligible fiscal impact.
1.1.1.1.2.1. Pro: A wide variety of [meta-analyses and studies](https://www.cato.org/sites/cato.org/files/pubs/pdf/working-paper-21-fix.pdf) have never demonstrated that immigration has ever presented an undue burden on state or government budgets.
1.1.1.1.2.2. Pro: It is widely accepted that immigrants present a [massive boon](https://d279m997dpfwgl.cloudfront.net/wp/2016/09/0922_immigrant-economics-full-report.pdf) to economic activity.
1.1.1.1.2.3. Pro: The benefits of immigrants are accepted even by fervently [anti-immigration economists](https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2016/09/trump-clinton-immigration-economy-unemployment-jobs-214216).
1.1.1.1.2.4. Pro: All economies not only require skilled workers, but the labourers to bring these skilled workers' ambitions to fruition. If we take the argument that President Trump managed an 'economic miracle', he would have needed an increased supply of labour to facilitate this expansion.
1.1.1.1.3. Con: The vast majority of illegal immigration into the United States does not come from border-crossing, but from people [overstaying their visas](https://www.cnbc.com/2019/01/08/despite-trumps-claims-most-illegal-immigration-is-not-at-the-southern-border.html). President Trump has done a poorer job addressing this than Obama.
1.1.1.1.4. Con: The illegal immigrant population has been [steadily declining since its peak in 2007](https://www.pewresearch.org/hispanic/2018/11/27/u-s-unauthorized-immigrant-total-dips-to-lowest-level-in-a-decade/). There is no evidence that President Trump did significantly decrease it. The primary focus of President Trump's policies was to [restrict legal immigration](https://www.afsc.org/blogs/news-and-commentary/trumps-attacks-legal-immigration-system-explained), including both legal asylum seekers and [high-skill immigrants](https://www.nytimes.com/2020/06/22/us/politics/trump-h1b-work-visas.html) who greatly [benefit the economy](https://www.bushcenter.org/publications/resources-reports/reports/immigration.html?gclid=Cj0KCQjw9IX4BRCcARIsAOD2OB1_G9Bu322Loe5zvdpReymVsPWGJaCgXdrcho0giJTwKXLVIbAhpmoaAuJiEALw_wcB) by working hard and [starting companies](https://www.forbes.com/sites/stuartanderson/2018/10/25/55-of-americas-billion-dollar-startups-have-immigrant-founder/#34c2473548ee) that employ Americans.
1.1.1.2. Con: There is no evidence that illegal immigration rates have reduced since President Trump was sworn into office.
1.1.1.2.1. Con: From 2017 to 2019, there was an [increase in the number of detentions at the borders](https://www.bbc.com/news/election-us-2020-54638643).
1.1.1.2.2. Pro: The number of unauthorized immigrants in the US started to decline [before Trump's administration](https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2019/06/12/us-unauthorized-immigrant-population-2017/ft_19-06-12_unauthorizedimmigration_number-unauthorized-immigrants-in-us-declined_corrected/).
1.1.1.3. Con: President [Trump's immigration policies](https://www.thenation.com/article/archive/trumps-war-on-migrants-is-an-affront-to-humanity/) were cruel and hurtful and did not serve the interests of compassion, diversity, and humanity.
1.1.1.3.1. Pro: President Trump's immigration policies encouraged [family separation](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/early-childhood/reports/2018/07/12/453378/trumps-family-incarceration-policy-threatens-healthy-child-development/).
1.1.1.3.2. Pro: President Trump almost eliminated [asylum in the US](https://www.rescue.org/article/how-trump-administration-eliminating-asylum-us)(Under President Trump, seeking and receiving safety in the United States has become next to impossible.).
1.1.1.3.3. Pro: There have been cases of [coerced sterilization](https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2020/09/25/ice-is-accused-sterilizing-detainees-that-echoes-uss-long-history-forced-sterilization/) at immigration detention centers.
1.1.1.3.4. Con: Many of President Trump's immigration policies were [continuations](https://www.vox.com/2018/6/21/17488458/obama-immigration-policy-family-separation-border) of Obama-era policies.
1.1.1.3.5. Pro: Refugee admissions into the US [fell drastically under Trump's presidency](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/election-us-2020-54638643)(The number of people admitted to the US as refugees each year is determined by a system of quotas, the size of which are ultimately defined by the president. People seeking to move to the US as refugees must make their applications from outside the country, and need to convince US officials that they are vulnerable to persecution at home.\n\nMr Trump's hostility to any immigration from Muslim-majority countries is well known - he once pledged to enact a "complete shutdown of Muslims entering the United States" - and a reduction in refugee quotas proved easier to implement than an outright ban, which became mired in legal challenges.\n\nAs a result, the number of refugees admitted from a number of majority-Muslim countries, including Iraq, Somalia, Iran and Syria, fell almost to zero soon after he took office.).
1.1.1.4. Pro: From 2016 to July 2020, President Trump [reduced legal immigration](https://www.forbes.com/sites/stuartanderson/2020/07/21/trump-cuts-legal-immigrants-by-half-and-hes-not-done-yet/#4a6bee5c6168) by 49%.
1.1.1.5. Con: Reducing legal immigration is not aligned with American values.
1.1.2. Con: President Trump was unable to combat COVID-19 effectively.
1.1.2.1. Pro: [On February 8th, 2020, the CDC produced thousands of failed tests](https://www.rollingstone.com/politics/politics-features/covid-19-test-trump-admin-failed-disaster-995930/) that would have slowed the virus and allowed for tracing and fewer restrictions of who could be tested.
1.1.2.2. Pro: During Trump's presidency, the US had one of the world's [highest mortality rates](https://edition.cnn.com/2020/07/20/politics/donald-trump-coronavirus-mortality-rate-intl/index.html)(But the President's claim is not true. And it's not even close.\n\nThe US in fact has one of the highest death rates from the coronavirus of any country, and is worse than several badly-hit countries like Brazil, Mexico and Russia, according to data collected by Johns Hopkins University.) from COVID-19.
1.1.2.2.1. Con: One-third of the death count came from California, [New York](https://www.google.com/search?sxsrf=ALeKk00FNoc65HLDXxvwv6CWSlxC6rTTjw%3A1600895716213&ei=5LprX6PDDMq4tQbSkqbQBQ&q=new+york+coronavirus+death+count+today&oq=new+york+coronavirus+death+count+today&gs_lcp=CgZwc3ktYWIQAzIECCMQJzoGCAAQBxAeOgQIABANOggIABANEAUQHjoHCCMQsAIQJ1ClyQFYv-MBYNXnAWgCcAB4AIABUIgBowaSAQIxMZgBAKABAaoBB2d3cy13aXrAAQE&sclient=psy-ab&ved=0ahUKEwijxfKjmYDsAhVKXM0KHVKJCVoQ4dUDCA0&uact=5), and [New Jersey](https://www.google.com/search?sxsrf=ALeKk0057FH1ZilJvm9cY1Fnr5DOckEnow%3A1600896109339&ei=bbxrX7SOFMq4tAaN5o3YCw&q=new+jersey+coronavirus+death+count+today&oq=new+jersey+coronavirus+death+count+today&gs_lcp=CgZwc3ktYWIQAzIECCMQJzoGCAAQBxAeOgcIIxCwAhAnULMjWNI0YK84aABwAHgAgAFIiAGRBZIBAjEwmAEAoAEBqgEHZ3dzLXdpesABAQ&sclient=psy-ab&ved=0ahUKEwj0-KzfmoDsAhVKHM0KHQ1zA7sQ4dUDCA0&uact=5). President Trump didn't control anything in these federated, Democrat-run cities. This was scape-goating and indicated that the Democrats were unable to handle a health crisis.
1.1.2.2.2. Pro: The U.S. had the highest COVID-19 death rate recorded in high-income countries and led the world in the number of total pandemic deaths with [214,776](https://www.emsworld.com/news/1225033/us-has-highest-covid-19-death-rate-developed-world). \(October 2020\).
1.1.2.3. Con: It was on everyone to not spread the virus - the president and government did their job by providing information.
1.1.2.3.1. Con: [The Trump administration closed testing centers in communities where cases were spiking.](https://www.npr.org/sections/coronavirus-live-updates/2020/06/24/883154244/trump-administration-moving-to-close-federally-funded-covid-testing-sites)
1.1.2.3.2. Con: President Trump [admitted](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-54094559) that he downplayed the seriousness of the virus from the start. He should have been more upfront about it and taken proper measures.
1.1.2.3.2.1. Pro: [Since late February 2020](https://edition.cnn.com/2020/02/27/politics/trump-coronavirus-disappear/index.html), President Trump insisted the virus would magically disappear.
1.1.2.3.2.2. Con: Other [world leaders](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-10-02/three-leaders-downplayed-covid-and-ended-up-catching-it) also downplayed the virus from the start.
1.1.2.3.3. Pro: [88% of Americans](https://www.pewresearch.org/politics/2020/05/12/most-americans-say-federal-government-has-primary-responsibility-for-covid-19-testing/) said in May 2020 that hospitals, health officials, and local officials did well responding to COVID-19.
1.1.2.3.4. Con: Some of the information provided by president Trump was dangerously inaccurate.
1.1.2.3.4.1. Pro: President Trump incorrectly suggested that [injecting patients with disinfectant might help treat COVID-19](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-52407177)(US President Donald Trump has been lambasted by the medical community after suggesting research into whether coronavirus might be treated by injecting disinfectant into the body.\n\nHe also appeared to propose irradiating patients' bodies with UV light, an idea dismissed by a doctor at the briefing.\n\nAnother of his officials had moments earlier said sunlight and disinfectant were known to kill the infection.\n\nDisinfectants are hazardous substances and can be poisonous if ingested.\n\nEven external exposure can be dangerous to the skin, eyes and respiratory system.).
1.1.2.4. Con: President Trump's [COVID-19 plan](https://www.whitehouse.gov/openingamerica/) is echoed in [Joe Biden's plan](https://joebiden.com/covid19/#).
1.1.2.5. Con: President Trump [closed down the US](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-51846923) almost immediately when COVID-19 was announced by the [WHO](https://www.who.int/news/item/27-04-2020-who-timeline---covid-19).
1.1.2.5.1. Con: The US wasn't the only country to close down, as many other countries also imposed [travel restrictions and bans](https://www.nytimes.com/article/coronavirus-travel-restrictions.html).
1.1.2.5.1.1. Pro: President Trump's travel ban restrictions [came too late](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/coronavirus-cdc-latest-trump-travel-ban-where-covid-come-from-europe-a9623721.html) compared to other [European restrictions](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-51892477).
1.1.2.5.1.2. Con: President Trump reacted efficiently as he imposed the measures on the [same day that the World Health Organization](https://www.statnews.com/2020/03/11/trump-europe-travel-ban/)(WASHINGTON — President Trump on Wednesday said the United States would suspend travel from Europe for 30 days, a dramatic escalation of the federal government’s response to the coronavirus outbreak.\n\nThe measures come the same day that the World Health Organization declared the outbreak a global pandemic. Already, U.S. health officials have recorded over 1,000 cases of the novel coronavirus and the respiratory disease it causes, known as Covid-19. Worldwide cases exceed 125,000, nearly 5,000 of which have been fatal.) declared the outbreak a global pandemic.
1.1.2.5.2. Pro: The White House released a list of [President Trump’s historic COVID-19 responses](https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefings-statements/president-trumps-historic-coronavirus-response/).
1.1.2.5.3. Con: On [January 31st, 2020](https://www.hhs.gov/about/news/2020/01/31/secretary-azar-declares-public-health-emergency-us-2019-novel-coronavirus.html), COVID-19 was declared a public health emergency in the US. President Trump declared a national emergency on [March 13th](https://www.whitehouse.gov/presidential-actions/proclamation-declaring-national-emergency-concerning-novel-coronavirus-disease-covid-19-outbreak/) and granted [$42 billion](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2020/03/13/coronavirus-bill-house-nears-approval-free-tests-paid-sick-leave/5039259002/) to fight COVID-19.
1.1.2.5.3.1. Pro: President Trump delayed taking necessary steps by [up to six weeks](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/mar/28/trump-coronavirus-politics-us-health-disaster) in some instances.
1.1.2.5.3.1.1. Pro: Less than three weeks after telling [Bob Woodward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Woodward) the disease was [very scary and deadlier than the flu](https://abcnews.go.com/Politics/president-trump-coronavirus-versus-bob-woodward-recorded-interviews/story?id=72912827), he repeatedly downplayed the threat to the American people and postponed lockdowns.
1.1.2.5.3.2. Pro: Most Americans think President Trump was too slow with his "[initial response to COVID-19 threat.](https://www.pewresearch.org/politics/2020/04/16/most-americans-say-trump-was-too-slow-in-initial-response-to-coronavirus-threat/)"
1.1.2.5.3.3. Con: Most European countries didn't declare COVID-19 a national emergency until [March 2020](https://www.politico.eu/article/europes-coronavirus-lockdown-measures-compared/).
1.1.2.5.4. Pro: President Trump placed a [30-day travel ban on March 2020](https://www.politico.eu/article/coronavirus-donald-trump-europe-travel-ban-explained/) on anyone who had been to the European Schengen area, in order to prevent further spread of COVID-19.
1.1.2.6. Con: President Trump's actions during the first year of COVID-19 indicated how committed he was to fighting the crisis.
1.1.2.6.1. Con: President Trump's actions caused COVID-19 to become a pandemic with his [abroad](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-health-coronavirus-china-cdc-exclusiv/exclusive-u-s-slashed-cdc-staff-inside-china-prior-to-coronavirus-outbreak-idUSKBN21C3N5) and [local](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/mar/24/trump-cuts-undermine-coronavirus-containment-cdc-watchdog-report) staff cuts.
1.1.2.6.1.1. Pro: President Trump [cut funding from the WHO](https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-cutting-who-funding-amid-coronavirus-could-cost-american-lives-2020-4) and [canceled an order of 80,000 ventilators](https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/26/us/politics/coronavirus-ventilators-trump.html) because the price \($1 billion\) was 'too unrealistic'.
1.1.2.6.1.1.1. Con: With so many scams going on \(like the [fake PPE](https://www.sbsun.com/2020/04/27/coronavirus-riverside-and-rancho-cucamonga-men-arrested-on-suspicion-of-defrauding-ppe-distributors/)\), it makes sense to be cautious and figure out what makes sense before jumping in only to find out it isn't needed as much. There might've been something better and cheaper with what he was thinking, but we won't know if people think about why he thought it was too expensive, rather than what was his alternative.
1.1.2.6.1.2. Con: COVID-19 was a [pandemic](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-51839944) everywhere in the world independently of President Trump's actions.
1.1.2.6.1.2.1. Con: The United States was about to enter a [major economic crisis because of COVID-19](https://www.vox.com/2020/3/9/21167391/coronavirus-economy-stimulus-recession), but President Trump was dealing with the pandemic by going into denial.
1.1.2.6.1.2.1.1. Pro: The number of COVID-19 cases in the United States is [rapidly growing](https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/05/world/coronavirus-live-updates.html).
1.1.2.6.1.2.1.2. Pro: President Trump suffered the consequences of this denial in the 2020 presidential elections.
1.1.2.6.1.3. Pro: President Trump's [staff cuts](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/mar/24/trump-cuts-undermine-coronavirus-containment-cdc-watchdog-report) undermined COVID-19 containment efforts back at the beginning of the pandemic.
1.1.2.6.1.4. Con: According to the [White House](http://President Trump led the largest mobilization of public and private sector resources since WWII.), President Trump "led the largest mobilization of public and private sector resources since WWII."
1.1.2.6.2. Pro: President Trump's increased Department of Defense spending contributed to the ability to run [Operation Warp Speed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Warp_Speed), from May 15, 2020, with the aim of developing COVID-19 vaccine candidates faster and more effectively than private venture could.
1.1.2.6.2.1. Pro: Thanks to [Operation Warp Speed and the allocated $14 billion](https://www.insideover.com/politics/operation-warp-speed-trumps-covid-success.html), President Trump ensured that the authorities, scientists, and companies’ efforts led to more unity in achieving the goal to find a vaccine.
1.1.2.6.2.2. Con: The Operation Warp Speed failed to [provide the promised deliveries of doses](https://www.politico.com/news/2021/01/17/crash-landing-of-operation-warp-speed-459892) and quickly exhausted [reserve supplies.](https://www.washingtonpost.com/health/2021/01/15/trump-vaccine-reserve-used-up/)
1.1.2.6.3. Pro: President Trump [donated](https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/03/trump-donates-his-2019-q4-salary-to-help-combat-coronavirus.html) his 4th quarter salary for 2019 to fight the pandemic.
1.1.2.6.4. Pro: President Trump [moved the tax filing date](https://apnews.com/article/2c64a8ff22ddc61ffce4bd52ffd020ef) from April 15 to July 15 2020 in order to provide relief to Americans during the pandemic.
1.1.2.6.5. Pro: On March 27th, 2020, President Trump signed the [CARES Act](https://www.cnbc.com/2020/03/27/house-passes-2-trillion-coronavirus-stimulus-bill-sends-it-to-trump.html), a COVID-19 relief bill of $2 trillion to prevent economic devastation.
1.1.2.6.6. Con: Trump [knew how serious the virus was](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-54094559) and hid the truth, downplaying the virus and doing nothing.
1.1.2.6.6.1. Pro: If Trump had taken the virus seriously; the death toll would be [notably less](https://www.reuters.com/article/uk-health-coronavirus-usa-idUKKBN2BK0RG).
1.1.2.6.6.2. Con: Information was available to the public about the dangers of the virus from other reputable [domestic](https://www.cdc.gov/coronavirus/2019-ncov/php/infection-control.html)(Preventing the Spread of COVID-19 in a Variety of Settings Throughout Your Community\n\nGuidance About Preventing COVID-19 Infections in Diverse Settings) and [international](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/health-54648684)(A simple virus has brought life as we know it to a screeching halt.\n\nWe have faced viral threats before, including pandemics, yet the world does not shut down for every new infection or flu season.\n\nSo what is it about this coronavirus? What are the quirks of its biology that pose a unique threat to our bodies and our lives?) sources.
1.1.2.7. Con: President Trump handled some health crises well.
1.1.2.7.1. Pro: President Trump declared a [state of emergency for opioid addiction](https://www.whitehouse.gov/opioids/) which provided funding and a dedicated task force.
1.1.2.7.1.1. Con: A report from 2018 concluded that the [emergency declaration didn't have many positive results](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2018/10/23/18010304/trump-opioid-epidemic-emergency-gao-report)(A new report from the Government Accountability Office \(GAO\) looked at the results of that emergency declaration. The report found little came out of the declaration.).
1.1.2.7.1.2. Pro: Positive outcomes have included [prescription monitoring programs](https://bmchealthservres.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s12913-019-4642-8)(rug monitoring programs \(PDMPs\) aim to increase patient safety by certifying that opioids are prescribed in appropriate quantities.) and expanded treatment.
1.1.3. Pro: President Trump gave much more freedom \(allowing people the liberty to do things on their own accord\) to Americans and the local government compared to other presidents.
1.1.3.1. Pro: Compared to other presidents in recent years, President Trump adopted a 'hands-free' management approach to let the local government do what they wanted to do, such as in the case of the [pandemic](https://www.politico.com/news/2020/04/16/trump-plan-for-reopening-economy-191073).
1.1.3.2. Con: President Trump didn't give the same freedom to all Americans, since he strengthened [racial division](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/meet-the-press/racial-division-hallmark-trump-s-presidency-n1030286).
1.1.3.3. Pro: President Trump pushed for [deregulation](https://www.brookings.edu/interactives/tracking-deregulation-in-the-trump-era/) during his administration, putting the responsibility of policymaking on the shoulders of the states, as intended in the US Constitution.
1.1.3.3.1. Pro: He [removed many regulations](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/has-trump-killed-more-regulations-than-any-other-president/), in keeping with his [campaign promises](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/promises/trumpometer/).
1.1.3.3.1.1. Con: Slashing environmental regulations is a terrible move which will lead to increased pollution, food poisoning, and so on.
1.1.3.3.1.2. Con: The consequences of [deregulation can destroy peoples](https://www.epi.org/blog/deregulation-can-kill-you/) lives, lands, and freedoms.
1.1.3.3.1.3. Pro: The Trump administration [started 514 deregulatory rulemakings](https://accf.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/03/ACCF-Report_Trump-Deregulatory-Record-FINAL.pdf) on a wide range of issues at different agencies. \(p. 26\)
1.1.3.3.1.4. Pro: Deregulation [increases](https://learn.robinhood.com/articles/3xnlbuG9QuGJtYeKlOlvf5/what-is-deregulation/) [free-market](https://learn.robinhood.com/articles/7Ium1gWWf54wd5wqr1XosD/what-is-a-free-market/) competition, giving consumers [more choice](https://www.investopedia.com/ask/answers/033015/what-are-some-advantages-market-economy-over-other-types-economies.asp).
1.1.3.3.1.5. Con: Removing regulations is only positive action when regulations do more harm than good. Blanket opposition to regulation can be highly destructive as many have been hard fought for and serve to protect citizens.
1.1.3.3.1.6. Con: President Trump honoring one promise didn't outweigh the numerous ways he reneged on promises or [lied during the campaign](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/fact-checker/wp/2018/08/01/president-trump-has-made-4229-false-or-misleading-claims-in-558-days/?utm_term=.81b1043098b2), and in office.
1.1.3.3.2. Con: [Deregulation](https://www.citizen.org/news/trumps-deregulation-push-is-setting-the-stage-for-major-national-disasters/) was merely used for President Trump's corporate greed. Voters did not ask for it.
1.1.3.3.3. Pro: According to the White House, Trump's administration reduced the size, scope, and cost of federal regulations for the first time in decades with [noticeable results](https://www.banking.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/The-Economic-Effects-of-Federal-Deregulation-Interim-Report.pdf).
1.1.3.3.4. Con: Deregulation can often increase [unhealthy risks taken by businesses](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/planetpolicy/2018/01/09/the-danger-in-deregulation/).
1.1.3.3.5. Con: Deregulation was a primary cause of the [2008 financial housing crisis](https://www.thebalance.com/what-caused-2008-global-financial-crisis-3306176#:~:text=Deregulation%20in%20the%20financial%20industry%20was%20the,of%20the%202008%20financial%20crash.&text=Since%20home%20loans%20were%20intimately,to%20its%20knees%20as%20well.).
1.1.3.3.6. Con: Some regulations must be equally placed on all participating members \(states\) to [ensure fair competition](https://www.mic.com/articles/3924/government-regulations-help-markets-work-better) in an open-market economy.
1.1.4. Con: President Trump passed insignificant legislation, which was also broadly ineffective.
1.1.4.1. Con: A President does not pass legislation. Therefore, no President has passed legislation.
1.1.4.1.1. Pro: [US Constitution, Article I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Article_One_of_the_United_States_Constitution) states that "all legislative Powers herein granted shall be vested in a Congress of the United States, which shall consist of a Senate and House of Representatives."
1.1.4.1.1.1. Con: The final step of passing a bill into law is directly the responsibility of the President. [They can pass, veto, or abstain from signing the laws.](https://www.usa.gov/how-laws-are-made)
1.1.4.1.1.2. Pro: When a representative sponsors a bill, it is then assigned to a committee for study. If released, it is then put on a calendar to be voted on \(by simple majority\), debated or amended. If voted, the [bill moves to the Senate](https://www.house.gov/the-house-explained/the-legislative-process).
1.1.4.1.2. Con: It is generally understood that a [President passes laws through Congress](https://www.whitehouse.gov/about-the-white-house/the-legislative-branch/). Many Presidents have passed laws.
1.1.4.2. Con: [President Trump signed the First Step Act into law](https://www.brennancenter.org/our-work/research-reports/what-first-step-act-and-whats-happening-it), marking the first legislative victory in years for advocates seeking to reform the criminal justice system at the federal level.
1.1.4.3. Con: President Trump passed the [VA Accountability Act](https://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2017/jun/23/donald-trump-signs-va-accountability-act-law-promi/), allowing the firing of civil servants who mistreat veterans.
1.1.4.3.1. Con: To call this 'significant' is stretching the meaning of the word.
1.1.4.4. Con: President Trump passed the [VA Mission Act](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2018/06/06/trump-signs-law-expanding-vets-healthcare-choices/673906002/), which allows veterans to see a private doctor if they've been waiting too long for treatment.
1.1.4.4.1. Con: -> See 1.1.4.3.1.
1.1.4.5. Pro: [A member within President Trump's administration](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/09/05/opinion/trump-white-house-anonymous-resistance.html) has branded his leadership style ineffective and his actual results non-existent.
1.1.4.5.1. Con: The NYT op-ed is an unacceptable attack on President Trump, possibly from what has been termed the 'deep state': [working and briefing against the President](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/09/05/opinion/trump-white-house-anonymous-resistance.html), and [attempting to thwart](http://nymag.com/daily/intelligencer/2018/08/peter-strzok-fired-from-fbi-over-anti-trump-texts.html) his democratic mandate.

Pro: Their [anonymous, cowardly, and narcissistic attacks](https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/people/2018/09/06/first-lady-melania-trump-condemns-anonymous-op-ed-writer-cowardly/1212385002/) have been [widely criticized on both the left and right.](https://observer.com/2018/09/why-democratic-strategist-are-slamming-the-anonymous-trump-op-ed/)

1.1.4.5.1.2.1. Pro: The [deep state](https://www.npr.org/2020/04/15/834874400/in-deep-challenges-president-trump-s-notion-of-a-deep-state-conspiracy) conspiracy theory came to prominence during President Trump's election and campaign and has been furthered by his supporters without evidence.
1.1.4.5.1.2.1.1. Pro: [TDS \(Trump Derangement Syndrome\)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump_derangement_syndrome)(Trump derangement syndrome \(TDS\) is a pejorative term usually for criticism or negative reactions to United States President Donald Trump that are perceived to be irrational, and have little regard towards Trump's actual policy positions, or actions undertaken by his administration.) is a label President Trump and his supporters commonly use.
1.1.4.5.1.2.1.1.1. Pro: Many [therapists claim](http://insider.foxnews.com/2018/07/30/psychiatrist-debunks-trump-anxiety-disorder-says-it-partisan-pop-psychology) there is no such thing as TAD or [TDS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump_Derangement_Syndrome) and it is instead "partisan pop psychology".

Even if there were anxiety, many would consider it [justifiable](https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/blog/talking-about-men/201901/is-trump-derangement-syndrome-real-mental-condition?page=1) given the President's actions.

1.1.4.10.5.2.1. Pro: Vice President Pence would deliver whatever statement painted his office and his party in the best light, as would every senior White House staff member. They were not beholden to the truth.
1.1.4.10.5.2.2. Con: This would not be the first time Bob Woodward got the wrong end of the stick. His biography on John Belushi was [criticised](https://www.washingtonpost.com/archive/lifestyle/1984/06/04/friends-of-belushi-criticize-wired/7c394846-1b6a-4702-a79a-83534acd1102/?noredirect=on&utm_term=.1224cdc045d3) as "unfair," "humorless" and "depressing", and which a subsequent biographer found [very troubling.](https://amp.slate.com/articles/arts/culturebox/2013/03/bob_woodward_and_gene_sperling_what_woodward_s_john_belushi_book_can_tell.html)
1.1.4.10.5.2.2.1. Con: This is less an example of Bob Woodward getting a story “completely wrong” and more an example of two writers having different attitudes about the subject. The writer of the article above even acknowledges that Woodward was generally correct with the facts, but assembled them to the wrong overall story in their mind.
1.1.4.10.5.2.2.1.1. Pro: A quote from the article explains that this book is not a great representation of Woodward’s overall body of work: “Wired is an anomaly in the Woodward catalog, the only book he’s ever written about a subject other than Washington.“
1.1.4.10.5.3. Con: [Bob Woodward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Woodward) was neither anonymous \(though admittedly, his sources were\), nor lacked credibility.
1.1.4.10.5.4. Pro: UN Ambassador and former Governor Nikki Haley [said that](https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/policy/defense-national-security/nikki-haley-take-bob-woodwards-book-with-a-grain-of-salt)(“I know that the president has been a great partner to me on foreign security. I meet with him often. I talk with him often. When I have concerns, I bring them to him. He listens, he's respectful, and he engages back.”) Woodward's book should have been taken with a grain of salt'.
1.1.4.10.5.5. Pro: President Trump's lawyer, Rudy Giuliani, [made the point](https://finance.yahoo.com/video/giuliani-says-diaper-anecdote-woodward-054236136.html) that Woodward's book included an unflattering anecdote involving him, which Giuliani claimed it was false. Woodward never tried to interview Giuliani about it and left Woodward open to the charge that he relied too much on second-hand accounts rather than primary sources.
1.1.4.10.5.5.1. Con: An 'unflattering anecdote' may well have been something Giuliani wished to distance himself from.
1.1.4.10.5.5.2. Con: Bob Woodward [claimed](https://www.comicsands.com/bob-woodward-has-the-receipts-2604988932.html?utm_content=inf_10_3759_2&utm_source=facebook&utm_campaign=GTAK&tse_id=INF_31e10a80b90f11e8872dc93302272904) to have tapes of all interviews and quotes and said he would release them if anyone publicly asked or claimed to have been misquoted.
1.1.4.10.5.5.2.1. Pro: President Trump [claimed](https://talkingpointsmemo.com/news/trump-woodward-call) that he never spoke to Woodward in any capacity. While this was true for the content of the book, [Woodward](https://www.newsandguts.com/video/must-listen-bob-woodward-tapes-conversation-donald-trump/) [released](https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2018/09/04/transcript-phone-call-between-president-trump-journalist-bob-woodward/) a [tape](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pQ8aGoEYV2Y) [showing](https://www.cnn.com/2018/09/04/politics/bob-woodward-donald-trump-phone-call/index.html) that he did in fact speak to Trump just before the book's launch.
1.1.4.10.6. Pro: President Trump selected [Brett Kavanaugh](https://time.com/5417538/bett-kavanaugh-confirmed-senate-supreme-court/), a transparently partisan individual accused of rape and perjury, for the Supreme Court.
1.1.4.10.6.1. Con: The accusations against Kavanaugh were flimsy and likely fabricated.
1.1.4.10.6.1.1. Con: [Kavanaugh's sexual misconduct allegations](https://www.vox.com/2019/9/16/20868338/brett-kavanaugh-new-york-times-impeachment-allegations) led to new reporting in 2019, which led to calls for Kavanaugh’s impeachment.
1.1.4.10.6.1.2. Pro: Julie Swetnick's accusation lacked corroboration. She [changed her story](http://insider.foxnews.com/2018/10/02/guy-benson-julie-swetnick-brett-kavanaugh-allegation-nbc-news-interview), had a less than stellar [legal history](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/3rd-brett-kavanaugh-accuser-julie-swetnick-has-history-of-legal-disputes/), and had several people who knew her and attested to her [untrustworthy character.](https://nypost.com/2018/09/26/third-kavanaugh-accusers-ex-boyfriend-once-accused-her-of-domestic-violence/)
1.1.4.10.6.1.2.1. Con: Swetnick's affidavit "[adds credibility to the image of Kavanaugh](https://www.vox.com/identities/2018/9/26/17906130/brett-kavanaugh-julie-swetnick-renate-dolphin)(Her affidavit adds credibility to the image of Kavanaugh painted by Ford, Ramirez, and former Georgetown Prep and Yale University students: someone who repeatedly victimized women in his time at the elite institutions that ostensibly prepared him for his career.)" painted by the other women who accused him of sexual misconduct.
1.1.4.10.6.1.2.2. Pro: Swetnick was [referred to the Justice Department](https://edition.cnn.com/2018/10/25/politics/julie-swetnick-justice-department-judiciary-committee/index.html) in 2018.
1.1.4.10.6.2. Pro: It seems [very plausible](https://www.vox.com/2018/10/2/17927606/brett-kavanaugh-perjury-lied-congress) that Kavanaugh committed perjury.
1.1.4.10.6.2.1. Con: It is possible that Kavanaugh's legal team were the ones involved in the text messages. Without the texts themselves, it is not clear either way.
1.1.4.10.6.2.2. Con: In regards to the question of text messages in relation to Ramirez's accusation, Kavanaugh may have heard of the incoming accusation, even if he had no certainty it would emerge or knowledge of details. Kavanaugh could have interpreted the question of when he first heard of the accusations as when he had heard of the details.
1.1.4.10.6.2.2.1. Con: His claims to not know her outside of University however were shown to be false. They were bridesmaid and Groomsman at a wedding together and are pictured together in a photo.
1.1.4.10.6.2.3. Con: On the subject of drinking, Kavanaugh admitted to drinking too much, but [claimed never to have "blacked out"](https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/kavanaugh-says-he-never-blacked-out-from-drinking-yeah-right/2018/09/25/60bba4d4-c0f1-11e8-be77-516336a26305_story.html), referring to an alcohol-induced period of amnesia. Whether he experienced a black out is almost entirely a case of his own state of mind, and so impossible to prove.
1.1.4.10.6.2.3.1. Con: He also says he never drank [underage](https://www.vox.com/2018/9/26/17901076/brett-kavanaugh-drinking-high-school-sexual-assault-allegations). The legal drinking age at the time was 21. He was 18. Someone familiar with the law would realise it.
1.1.4.10.6.2.3.2. Con: He carefully qualified that he never blacked out from drinking beer, and evasively never acknowledged or denied a possibility of blacking out from liquor, wine, or any other intoxicant.
1.1.4.10.6.2.4. Con: In terms of the yearbook slang, despite modern definitions differing from Kavanaugh's account, we had evidence that [boof can refer to flatulence](https://www.nationalreview.com/corner/brett-kavanaugh-meaning-of-boof/), we have a testimony and other yearbook entries that refer to FFFFF as an inside joke and devil's triangle as a game.
1.1.4.10.6.2.4.1. Con: We also have testimony from some of his other "friends" and classmates that he lied about these definitions, the same with Rentate Alumnus.
1.1.4.10.6.2.5. Con: In the case of the stolen Democratic emails, this is a question of a state of mind. If Kavanaugh claimed that he did not notice their origins, proof is required. Perhaps a documented reference to the stolen emails as stolen would suffice, but none have appeared. As such, this does not meet the grounds for perjury.
1.1.4.10.6.2.6. Pro: He claimed that he didn't have time for parties and never attended any. His own calendar shows at least 2, if not 3 in that one month.
1.1.4.10.6.2.7. Pro: Justice Kavanaugh clearly committed perjury when explaining the meaning of a [Devil's Triangle](https://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=Devils%20Triangle) while under oath during the Senate hearing of his nomination.
1.1.4.11. Con: President Trump also removed the [Obamacare individual mandate](https://www.cnbc.com/2018/01/30/trump-touts-repeal-of-obamacare-individual-mandate.html), which was the key objection of Republicans to Obamacare.
1.1.4.11.1. Pro: He repealed by [executive order](https://edition.cnn.com/2017/10/12/politics/trump-obamacare-executive-order/index.html)(President Donald Trump took his first steps Thursday toward fulfilling his vow to dismantle Obamacare, signing an executive order that he says will bring affordable health insurance to millions more people.\n\nThe order broadly tasks the administration with developing policies to increase health care competition and choice in order to improve the quality of health care and lower prices.) elements of the Affordable Healthcare Act that cost Americans a fortune.
1.1.4.11.1.1. Con: [He failed to replace it with anything meaningful](https://ballotpedia.org/Affordable_Care_Act_under_the_Trump_administration)(The House passed its bill—the American Health Care Act of 2017—but members of the Senate have been unable to agree on a final replacement plan, leaving most of the provisions of the ACA in place. Republicans did take one step towards changing the ACA by eliminating the law's individual mandate, which took effect in January 2019.), which means he only fulfilled half a promise.
1.1.4.11.1.2. Con: The Affordable Healthcare Act lowered the growth of long-term spending and government costs by over [$1 trillion](http://www.urban.org/sites/default/files/publication/90471/2001288-the_evidence_on_recent_health_care_spending_growth_and_the_impact_of_the_affordable_care_act.pdf), due to the cost controls it included.
1.1.4.11.1.3. Pro: By [developing policies to increase health care competition and choice](https://www.govinfo.gov/content/pkg/ERP-2020/pdf/ERP-2020-chapter5.pdf), President Trump improved the quality of health care and lowered the prices. \(p.171\)
1.1.4.11.1.3.1. Con: Healthcare in America is still one of the [most expensive](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2018/mar/13/us-healthcare-costs-causes-drug-prices-salaries) in the world.
1.1.4.11.1.3.1.1. Pro: This cripples many lower and middle class families who cannot afford healthcare.
1.1.4.11.1.3.2. Pro: [The Trump Administration lowered prescription drug prices](https://trumpwhitehouse.archives.gov/issues/healthcare/), expanded access to affordable coverage, and allowed Americans to access trusted doctors.
1.1.4.11.1.4. Pro: President Trump [included a provision in his 2017 legislation to eliminate the ObamaCare penalt](https://thehill.com/opinion/healthcare/385722-trump-has-quietly-saved-millions-from-obamacares-individual-mandate/)y, which cost $695 per adult or 2.5% of household income.
1.1.4.11.1.4.1. Con: Millions of people could lose their health insurance as a result of this repeal, many of them [could die](https://www.washingtonpost.com/posteverything/wp/2017/01/23/repealing-the-affordable-care-act-will-kill-more-than-43000-people-annually/).
1.1.4.11.1.4.1.1. Con: The people who will lose health insurance are those who do not want health insurance.
1.1.4.11.1.4.1.1.1. Con: The people who would lose health insurance would be [those that can't afford it](https://www.kff.org/uninsured/issue-brief/key-facts-about-the-uninsured-population/).
1.1.4.11.1.4.1.2. Pro: High deductible insurance was causing many people to forgo healthcare and [important medications](https://www.health.harvard.edu/blog/millions-skip-medications-due-to-their-high-cost-201501307673).
1.1.4.12. Con: President Trump [secured initial funding](https://www.texastribune.org/2018/03/23/donald-trump-border-wall-16-million-funding-restrictions-attached/) for building a wall on the border with Mexico in 2018.
1.1.4.12.1. Con: President Trump failed to build a wall and make Mexico [pay for it](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/promises/trumpometer/promise/1397/build-wall-and-make-mexico-pay-it/).
1.1.4.12.1.1. Pro: Not only was there no funding secured for building a wall, but President Trump also later denied he had ever claimed that [Mexico would be paying for the wall](https://time.com/5499391/donald-trump-border-wall-mexico-pay/).
1.1.4.12.1.2. Pro: "I will build a great wall – and nobody builds walls better than me, believe me – and I’ll build them very inexpensively. I will build a great, great wall on our southern border, and I will make Mexico pay for that wall. Mark my words.” - [No element](https://qz.com/1172972/trumps-border-wall-keeps-getting-shorter-and-more-expensive/) of this was truthful, and it was ostensibly arrogant.
1.1.4.12.1.3. Con: [It was reported](https://youtu.be/LiaiL-dHIDQ) that the US and Mexico were in the process of finalizing a trade deal that was more advantageous to the US than the previous one, which could have resulted in more tax revenue flowing in the US government coffers.
1.1.4.12.1.3.1. Con: A trade deal with Mexico favoring the US didn't mean that Mexico would end up paying for the wall, the two are separate matters.
1.1.4.12.2. Pro: The Trump administration notified Congress in February 2018 of its plans to divert [$3.8 billion from the Defense Department's budget](https://www.npr.org/2020/02/13/805796618/trump-administration-diverts-3-8-billion-in-pentagon-funding-to-border-wall) to build the border wall.
1.1.4.12.3. Con: A border wall is an ineffective measure, given [tunnels](https://www.cnn.com/2018/08/23/us/drug-tunnel-arizona-mexico-trnd/index.html) and [sea routes](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/immigrants-turn-to-sea-to-enter-us-illegally/).
1.1.4.12.4. Con: The wall was considered to likely be [ineffective](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/president-trump-executive-order-mexican-border-wall-impact/), according to many border patrol agents, and also [hinder them](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/border-patrol-officers-us-mexico-border-wall/) in doing their job by restricting viability and line of sight, among other issues.
1.1.4.12.4.1. Pro: The wall has had many [unintended side-effects](https://www.usatoday.com/border-wall/).
1.1.4.12.4.2. Pro: The [effectiveness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump_wall#Effectiveness) of [the wall](https://journalistsresource.org/studies/government/immigration/border-walls-barriers-fences-research/) is [still debatable](https://www.rand.org/blog/2019/01/what-border-walls-can-and-cannot-accomplish.html), [considered to be equal](https://www.aeaweb.org/research/border-wall-effectiveness-ben-feigenberg) to other equally costed measures, [with many considering](https://www.cato.org/publications/commentary/why-wall-wont-work) it a [waste of time](https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/trumps-border-wall-was-a-complete-waste-of-time-and-money/2020/12/24/444c165e-4564-11eb-b0e4-0f182923a025_story.html).
1.1.4.12.4.3. Con: [Some sources suggest](https://www.cbp.gov/frontline/border-security) the wall to be [effective](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump_wall#Effectiveness) and working, though [the impartiality of these sources was disputed](https://www.dhs.gov/news/2020/10/29/border-wall-system-deployed-effective-and-disrupting-criminals-and-smugglers#:~:text=CBP%20has%20seen%2079%25%20decrease,wall%20system%20in%20this%20area.).
1.1.5. Pro: President Trump's foreign policy achievements demonstrated that he was a good president.
1.1.5.1. Con: Something that seems to be good for the USA in the short term does not necessarily mean it is good for the USA in the long term. Long term ramifications are likely to weaken the USA in a variety of areas.
1.1.5.1.1. Pro: Warming and thawing relations with Russia, while a good goal of peace, is meaningless when it is demonstrated and shown they have not changed the ways [that got those sanctions imposed](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/row/R45415.pdf) in the first place.
1.1.5.1.1.1. Pro: [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_involvement_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War) continued to support the Syrian regime of [Bashar Al-Assad](https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/blogs/syriasource/three-years-later-the-evolution-of-russia-s-military-intervention-in-syria/), despite [his use of illegal chemical weapons](https://www.opcw.org/documents-related-syria).
1.1.5.1.2. Pro: Criticizing NATO, NATO Allies and thinking of reducing the NATO budget will weaken ties and trust among the organisation, thus weakening the partnership, which could cause problems in the future.
1.1.5.1.2.1. Con: This is a slippery slope argument. While criticising NATO could weaken ties and trust, it does not necessarily mean it will create a chain reaction of weakening NATO itself, which will then lead to problems of the future.
1.1.5.1.2.2. Pro: His [attacks on the WHO](https://uk.yahoo.com/news/coronavirus-donald-trumps-criticism-world-health-organisation-response-225700111.html) were generally rebuffed by the rest of the economically developed nations. Withholding funding and sowing doubt and mistrust will likely have long-term consequences.
1.1.5.1.2.3. Pro: We are already seeing some of those problems in Europe, Eastern Europe and Turkey.
1.1.5.1.2.3.1. Pro: [Turkey has bought Russian](https://www.cnn.com/2019/07/13/europe/turkey-russia-missiles-nato-analysis-intl/index.html) [Anti-Air and Missile Defence Systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S-400_missile_system), causing a [possibly irreconcilable](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-48620087) [rift within NATO](https://www.cnbc.com/2019/12/02/turkeys-arms-deal-with-russia-casts-shadow-over-nato-summit.html), [in defiance of the US](https://www.nytimes.com/2019/07/12/world/europe/turkey-russia-missiles.html). [This also](https://www.vox.com/world/2019/4/11/18292070/usa-turkey-trump-erdogan-s400) [stalled defense contracts and partnerships with the US](https://www.defensenews.com/air/2019/07/17/turkey-officially-kicked-out-of-f-35-program/).
1.1.5.1.2.3.2. Con: The current war in Ukraine shows that NATO could be a [threat for the European security](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-61369963).
1.1.5.1.2.3.2.1. Pro: [Europe no longer feels it can rely on the United States](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/aug/27/europe-can-no-longer-rely-on-us-for-security-says-emmanuel-macron) [in any role](https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/387067-merkel-europe-cant-count-on-us-to-protect-us-anymore) - [diplomatic](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-44045957) [partner](https://www.nytimes.com/2019/08/20/us/politics/trump-russia-g7.html) [in many roles](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2019/aug/25/g7-trumps-demands-for-russias-readmission-causes-row-in-biarritz), [trade](https://fortune.com/2019/10/14/us-eu-trade-war-airbus-vs-boeing-wto-gives-okay-us-7-5-billion-eu-import-tariffs/) [partner](https://www.euractiv.com/section/economy-jobs/news/the-impact-of-us-sanctions-on-european-goods-a-closer-look/) or for [security,](https://www.politico.eu/article/europe-defense-macron-cant-depend-on-us-for-security/) and [as such feels](https://warontherocks.com/2020/03/europes-defense-debate-is-all-about-america/) [it needs a](https://www.ft.com/content/51ed8b90-43b9-11e7-8519-9f94ee97d996) [United European Army instead of NATO](https://foreignpolicy.com/2019/09/05/europe-is-ready-for-its-own-army/) \([though many analysts forecast it will not be able to do so, only complement it](https://www.google.com/search?rlz=1C1CHBF_enCA843CA843&sxsrf=ALeKk03fWLv_Ytt5Xv2bt-dMz0OmkrNyqA%3A1588212051789&ei=UzGqXuTVL4aUtAaQzpqYDw&q=european+army+to+replace+nato&oq=european+army+&gs_lcp=CgZwc3ktYWIQAxgAMgQIIxAnMgIIADICCAAyAggAMgIIADICCAAyAggAMgIIADICCAAyAggAOgQIABBHOgYIABAWEB5Q3skCWLDYAmDF6QJoAHACeACAAZ4BiAGHDJIBBDAuMTGYAQCgAQGqAQdnd3Mtd2l6&sclient=psy-ab)\).
1.1.5.1.2.3.2.2. Con: [Eastern European](https://www.vox.com/2018/7/26/17614600/trump-nato-putin-summit-eastern-europe-criticism-response-reaction-poland-montenegro) countries felt [abandoned](https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2014/05/eastern-europe-vladimir-putin-107094) [by the US](https://apnews.com/4e0671ce3b1344f897122e9df1a7282e) [and NATO](https://foreignpolicy.com/2019/10/16/trump-abandoned-the-kurds-poland-and-the-baltics-could-be-next/), [under President Trump's leadership](https://www.atlanticcouncil.org/blogs/new-atlanticist/the-united-states-and-central-europe-what-s-gone-right-what-s-gone-wrong-and-what-s-next/), [in the face of](https://www.google.com/search?q=russia+invades+georgia&rlz=1C1CHBF_enCA843CA843&oq=Russia&aqs=chrome.0.69i59j69i57j46j0l2j69i60l3.3361j1j4&sourceid=chrome&ie=UTF-8) [renewed](https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/policy/defense-national-security/cutting-each-others-throats-allies-fear-russia-will-annex-belarus-to-save-putins-life) [Russian aggression](https://www.google.com/search?rlz=1C1CHBF_enCA843CA843&sxsrf=ALeKk01F9y1rSlyC_wAxJZhzoNhIPOVrUg%3A1588212788850&ei=NDSqXqezM-KE9PwP8pCkkA4&q=russia+annex+crimea&oq=russia+annex+crime&gs_lcp=CgZwc3ktYWIQAxgAMgQIABBDMgIIADICCAAyAggAMgYIABAWEB4yBggAEBYQHjIGCAAQFhAeMgYIABAWEB4yCAgAEBYQChAeMgYIABAWEB46BAgAEEdQp8QCWJvJAmCD0QJoAHAEeACAAcQDiAHGCpIBCTAuMi4xLjEuMZgBAKABAaoBB2d3cy13aXo&sclient=psy-ab).
1.1.5.1.3. Pro: Trump's behavior alienated many of America's traditional allies, such as [Canada](https://www.ctvnews.ca/politics/trump-slams-canada-on-twitter-suggests-replacing-nafta-with-separate-deals-1.3954972), [Britain](https://www.cnn.com/2018/05/05/politics/trump-nra-speech-angers-french/index.html), [Australia](https://www.cnn.com/2017/02/01/politics/malcolm-turnbull-donald-trump-pena-nieto/index.html), [Japan](https://www.newsweek.com/trump-abe-pearl-harbor-remember-ripped-trade-1093230), [Europe](https://nationalpost.com/news/world/trump-attacks-europes-refugee-policies-falsely-says-crime-in-germany-is-way-up) and most other members of [NATO](https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2018/07/09/donald-trump-slams-nato-allies-military-spending-ahead-leaving/). This was unlikely to be in America's best interests in the long run.
1.1.5.1.3.1. Con: [NATO is, in 2022, stronger than it was before](https://www.nato-pa.int/news/nato-allies-urged-boost-military-aid-ukraine-strengthen-eastern-flank-defences), which shows that President Trump's behavior didn't alienated traditional allies.
1.1.5.1.3.2. Pro: President Trump's actions also weakened ties with other countries, creating a space for other global powers such as [China](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/09/08/us/politics/us-latin-america-china.html) to replace the US.
1.1.5.1.3.3. Pro: The hegemony of the USA over the world is due to its alliances and standing with other modern, powerful countries. Damaging these relations would also damage its strength.
1.1.5.1.4. Con: [Since US Presidents are only elected for 4 years,](https://www.mentalfloss.com/article/633015/why-presidents-serve-four-year-terms) it is understandable that they would try to improve the country in the short term.
1.1.5.2. Con: President Trump's [actions](https://www.nbcnews.com/news/mideast/top-special-ops-marine-who-fought-kurds-blasts-trump-move-n1065901) to pull troops out of Syria in October 2019, led to further death and another situation where America betrayed its allies.
1.1.5.2.1. Pro: These actions threaten to [further empower ISIS](https://www.cnbc.com/2019/10/13/trump-defends-syria-withdrawal-amid-reports-of-atrocities-and-isis-supporters-escaping.html) as it was done without much planning and consultation with the US military or its allies.
1.1.5.2.2. Pro: President Trump's decision to pull out of Syria was widely condemned by even his [most ardent supporters](https://www.nytimes.com/2019/10/10/us/evangelicals-syria-trump-criticism.html).
1.1.5.2.3. Con: President Trump's decision to pull troops out of Syria was justified because he wanted to put an end to what he called [the United States’ role as a global policeman](https://www.rferl.org/a/trump-surprise-visit-u-s-troops-iraq/29678078.html).
1.1.5.3. Pro: President Trump left a good trade and diplomacy legacy.
1.1.5.3.1. Pro: President Trump's approach towards Russia was quite punitive.
1.1.5.3.1.1. Pro: Under President Trump, the US military killed 200 Russian soldiers [for crossing into US-controlled land in Syria](http://www.newsweek.com/us-military-killed-200-russians-syria-airstrikes-pompeo-says-trump-considers-883947).
1.1.5.3.1.1.1. Pro: It was considered the "[most lethal clash between US and Russian citizens since the end of the cold war](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/feb/13/russian-mercenaries-killed-us-airstrikes-syria)".

The sanctions "upheld" in January 2017 were [originally imposed by Obama](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2016/dec/29/barack-obama-sanctions-russia-election-hack), and those from August 2018 were pushed through by a [veto-proof majority](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/07/25/us/politics/fact-check-pompeo-sanctions-russia.html) in Congress.

Certainly, this was what President Trump repeatedly [said](https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefings-statements/president-donald-j-trump-acting-enforce-law-keeping-families-together/).

1.1.5.5.3.1.2. Con: If we knew President Trump's motivation, this would be a strong claim; however, motivation is a difficult thing to discern a priori, and we didn't know President Trump's motivation.
1.1.5.5.3.1.2.1. Pro: Moreover, [we cannot believe what he said](https://www.politifact.com/personalities/donald-trump/) most of the time, so his documented statements are of little use in determining what his motivations were.
1.1.5.5.3.2. Con: -> See 1.1.5.5.1.
1.1.5.5.3.3. Con: The crackdown on immigration from certain countries with significant internal problems linked with terrorism was [ruled constitutional](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-44619976) in 2018, and so it was neither inhumane nor racist.
1.1.5.5.3.3.1. Con: Under President Trump, the US took the [unprecedented step](https://secondnexus.com/news/geraldo-rivera-tear-gas-fox-news/?spot_im_reply_id=sp_8fvGl692_48092_c_14tpDX_r_hqWpqT&utm_spot=sp_8fvGl692&utm_source=SpotIM&utm_medium=E-mail&utm_content=liked-message) of firing tear gas, a chemical weapon, on an unarmed civilian refugee column, composed of a high percentage of women and children, across a border, onto foreign soil.
1.1.5.5.3.3.2. Con: If a policy is ruled as constitutional, it does not actually mean that it can't be racist or inhumane.
1.1.5.5.3.3.2.1. Pro: Upon constitutional founding, black people were worth [3/5ths](http://www.blackpast.org/aah/three-fifths-clause-united-states-constitution-1787) of a person. Many policies after the civil war have continued to either outright discriminate, or have been used overtly in discriminatory fashion.
1.1.5.5.3.3.3. Pro: The Constitution [protects human rights](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_United_States), and so for it to be ruled Constitutional meant that it was not an abuse of human rights.
1.1.5.5.3.4. Con: -> See 1.1.1.1.1.1.
1.1.5.5.3.5. Pro: The impact of his '[zero-tolerance](https://www.hrw.org/news/2018/08/16/qa-trump-administrations-zero-tolerance-immigration-policy)(new “zero-tolerance” policy intended to ramp-up criminal prosecution of people caught entering the United States illegally.)' policy, with increased levels of familial separation and unacceptable human rights abuses, was [very clear](https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/my-son-is-not-the-same-new-testimony-paints-bleak-picture-of-family-separation)(The motion filed Monday came with more than 900 pages of declarations that included powerful personal testimonies from parents, children and other family members who were directly impacted by the Trump policy. It also included declarations from the state attorneys general offices, elected representatives, advocates and child and immigration experts who have dealt with families separated at the border.).
1.1.5.5.3.5.1. Con: The clear impact is that America is slowly but surely stemming the flow of criminals into the country \([p. 1](https://www.ice.gov/sites/default/files/documents/Report/2017/iceEndOfYearFY2017.pdf)(The EO and implementation memorandum expanded ICE’s enforcement focus to include removable aliens who \(1\) have been convicted of any criminal offense; \(2\) have been charged with any criminal offense that has not been resolved; \(3\) have committed acts which constitute a chargeable criminal offense; \(4\) have engaged in fraud or willful misrepresentation in connection with any official matter before a governmental agency; \(5\) have abused any program related to receipt of public benefits; \(6\) are subject to a final order of removal but have not complied with their legal obligation to depart the United States; or \(7\) in the judgment of an immigration officer, otherwise pose a risk to public safety or national security. The Department has directed that classes or categories of removable aliens are no longer exempted from potential enforcement.)\).
1.1.5.5.3.5.1.1. Con: The numbers shown are [actually lower than previous years.](https://www.ice.gov/doclib/about/offices/ero/pdf/2013-ice-immigration-removals.pdf) This means that the policies are having no noticeable or observable effect and that if anything, the previous administration could take the credit.
1.1.5.5.3.6. Pro: President Trump made [false and misleading claims](https://www.factcheck.org/2018/04/trumps-chain-migration-fable/) about [chain migration](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2017/12/29/16504272/chain-migration-family-how-trump-end)(“Chain migration” is the technical name for a commonsense idea: People are more likely to move where their relatives are.).
1.1.5.5.3.6.1. Con: Chain immigration claims may have been exaggerated, but they were basically correct. The idea of having a lottery to let people into a country is questionable and President Trump was right to criticise it.
1.1.5.5.3.7. Pro: President Trump signed an executive order for a travel ban that [prohibited entry from seven countries](https://www.politico.com/interactives/2018/trump-travel-ban-supreme-court-decision-countries-map/)(Why are these countries being restricted?\n\nThe administration has cited poor cooperation with U.S. officials, terrorist activity and technical hurdles to properly document their own travelers as reasons for the latest iteration of the ban. In response, Trump sued O'Brien for libel and sought $5 billion in damages. While the courts ultimately dismissed the case for lacking merit, Trump said that he knew the lawsuit would fail but sued anyway. "I spent a couple of bucks on legal fees, and they spent a whole lot more. I did it to make his life miserable, which I'm happy about." Trump is not alone in using lawsuits, or the threat of lawsuits, to silence critics. Indeed, this has become such a problem in the United States that it is time for Congress to intervene, so that the court system does not merely become a tool to silence free speech among those who would speak out against powerful individuals and businesses.)".
