Trump \(\@realDonaldTrump\) April 5, 2019)" and popularized the phrase "[fake news](https://www.apnews.com/bc8b3670f9284186ac9a2699566b9baf)", thus deeply corroding the confidence in an age-old American institution.
1.2.1.4.1.1. Pro: President Trump attacked mainstream outlets as “enemies of the people” while he championed flattering coverage, such as the [One America News Network \(OAN\)](https://www.theguardian.com/tv-and-radio/2019/jun/15/oan-oann-fox-news-donald-trump)("The president rewards OAN with shout-outs and access wildly out of sync with its reach, leading some observers to suspect that he is playing OAN and Fox News off one another to ensure their undying affection.").
1.2.1.4.1.2. Con: In a democracy, [fake news exists](https://www.routledge.com/Post-Truth-Fake-News-and-Democracy-Mapping-the-Politics-of-Falsehood/Farkas-Schou/p/book/9780367322175), and President Trump should have been allowed to call out on what he perceived as fake news.
1.2.1.4.1.2.1. Con: As a President of a democratic society, President Trump should have respected [media freedom](https://freedomhouse.org/issues/media-freedom) and an independent, pluralistic media.
1.2.1.4.1.2.2. Pro: Calling out fake news is better than living in an [autocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autocracy)(Autocracy is a system of government in which supreme power over a state is concentrated in the hands of one person, whose decisions are subject to neither external legal restraints nor regularized mechanisms of popular control.), with no news and no freedom of speech.
1.2.1.4.1.3. Con: President Trump said that ["fake news" was the enemy of the people](https://thehill.com/homenews/administration/413764-trump-dishonest-to-say-i-called-all-media-enemy-of-the-people). He didn't call all media the enemy of the people.
1.2.1.4.1.3.1. Pro: President Trump stated at a rally in Florida in 2018 that a third of Americans believed that fake news was "[the enemy of the people](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-46053036)".
1.2.1.4.1.3.2. Con: President Trump also stated that 'fake news' was any news about him that he [disliked, disagreed with, or was otherwise negative about him.](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2018/5/9/17335306/trump-tweet-twitter-latest-fake-news-credentials)
1.2.1.4.1.3.2.1. Con: [Fox News’s Chris Wallace](https://www.cjr.org/special_report/coverage-trump-presidency-2020-election.php)(“Even if Trump is trying to undermine the press for his own calculated reasons,” Wallace said, “when he talks about bias in the media—unfairness—I think he has a point.”), who received an award for excellence in journalism in 2017, stated that when President Trump talked "about bias in the media", he had a point.
1.2.1.4.1.3.2.2. Pro: An organization or individual, belonging to the media, was only able to dodge the designation of "fake news" if they were in [regular private communication with the president, to ensure their messaging was beneficial to President Trump.](https://www.politico.eu/blogs/on-media/2018/07/sean-hannity-wins-as-donald-trumps-lone-defender-fox-news/)
1.2.1.4.2. Con: Press organisations that create [news for ratings and sensationalism](https://hbr.org/2017/01/the-u-s-medias-problems-are-much-bigger-than-fake-news-and-filter-bubbles) are not performing a public service.
1.2.1.4.3. Pro: To paint all major media outlets with a broad brush is dangerously misguided.
1.2.1.4.3.1. Pro: Not all news sources are equally good. Some have more professional staff and are less dependent on monetary incentives than others.
1.2.1.4.3.2. Pro: Media outlets' can be [biased](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_bias#Scholarly_treatment_in_the_United_States_and_United_Kingdom) in both their content and coverage. They would push a narrative that supports a particular side or publish half-truth or otherwise unequivocally false, details on stories that would push either sides' narrative. This goes against the goal of any good media organization, which is to publish unbiased coverage and factual content.
1.2.1.4.3.3. Pro: -> See 1.2.1.4.1.3.2.2.
1.2.1.4.4. Con: There are certain news organizations that spin content regarding the President in a biased light, which portrays an unflattering depiction of the President. He had a right to call out unfair content, or coverage of him.
1.2.1.4.4.1. Con: -> See 1.2.1.4.3.2.
1.2.1.4.4.2. Con: The President does have a right to call out half-truth content, but to portray the publishers of factual stories, based on the narrative of their coverage, as "fake news" sets a dangerous precedent.
1.2.1.4.4.3. Pro: Many mainstream sources pushed the narrative that the President called illegal/undocumented immigrants "animals".
1.2.1.4.4.3.1. Con: President Trump was consistently careless \(or deliberately ambiguous\) with the objects of his accusations.
1.2.1.4.4.3.1.1. Pro: Personal opinions are not what are asked of a president. His reasoning should be supported by evidences.
1.2.1.4.4.3.1.2. Pro: While making an argument against immigration, he usually talked about [MS-13](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/monkey-cage/wp/2018/12/07/trump-keeps-warning-about-ms-13-is-it-really-as-dangerous-as-he-suggests/) and started to hurling insults using pronouns, which is a common tactic to bring emotional heat into a discussion.
1.2.1.4.4.3.2. Pro: Many popular [news sources](https://www.bbc.com/future/article/20170301-lies-propaganda-and-fake-news-a-grand-challenge-of-our-age) don't specify the context in their titles, in a day and age when most people skim the titles of the news and share without reading the article.
1.2.1.4.4.3.3. Con: It is still unacceptable to call any person an animal regardless of context.
1.2.1.4.4.3.4. Pro: This is an unfair depiction of the [context of his discussion](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3tmT7-dhOWs), because he was referring to individuals under that subset that are in-and-out of the U.S. jail system, or repeat offenders.
1.2.1.4.4.3.5. Con: It's not hard to draw parallels from President Trump referring to immigrants as "[animals](https://lulac.org/news/pr/LULAC_Denounces_President_Trumps_Remarks_Calling_Undocumented_Immigrants_Animals/)" to Hitler calling Jews "[vermin](https://www.facinghistory.org/resource-library/image/when-vermin-are-dead-der-st-rmer-antisemitic-cartoon)" or the Hutus calling the Tutsis "[cockroaches](https://www.newtimes.co.rw/section/read/73836)" before those genocides. Even if Trump was using the term after MS-13 was mentioned, it's still a dangerous road to be on.
1.2.1.4.5. Pro: The press is an important check on both federal and local governments, as indicated by the inclusion of the [Freedom of the Press in the Bill of Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution).
1.2.1.4.5.1. Pro: The backbone of any democracy is an [independent, professional and responsible media](https://blogs.fcdo.gov.uk/petermillett/2012/02/13/the-responsibility-of-the-press/). Their role is to inform, criticise and stimulate debate.
1.2.1.4.5.1.1. Con: Not if they are creating news for channel ratings. [CNN](https://www.air.tv/watch?v=AFX3nmoNSL2imnmsZ6E6IA) got caught, but so many others reposted [CNN's "news" as real](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CNN_controversies) and never clarified which "news" was fake.
1.2.1.4.5.1.2. Pro: Media and investigative reporting have an important role in [deepening democracy](http://www.changecommunications.org/docs/dib/dibengunpan010194.pdf)(Investigative reporting, which in some cases has led to the ouster of presidents and the fall of corrupt governments, has made the media an effective and credible watchdog and boosted its credibility among the public). \(p.1\)
1.2.1.4.5.2. Pro: Undermining the public's trust in the veracity and intentions of the press as a whole is an underhanded maneuver of censoring it.
1.2.1.4.5.3. Con: Criticism is not the same as censorship.
1.2.1.4.5.3.1. Con: When criticizing a group of people whose livelihoods have been built on their reputation for reporting factual information, censorship undermines the infrastructure of their industry and their bottom line. The media industry is built off of views and impressions of the content produced. When people don't trust you, they don't view your material. If this were to continue for much longer, it could systematically censor them by eliminating the means of producing the content they create.
1.2.1.4.6. Con: It is the press [that has undermined](https://www.poynter.org/news/not-fake-news-just-plain-wrong-top-media-corrections-2017) the public's trust.
1.2.1.4.6.1. Con: The verbal disparagement and [threats](https://firstamendmentwatch.org/deep-dive/the-alarming-rise-in-verbal-and-physical-threats-to-the-press/) President Trump levied against the free press were dangerous and promoted unconstitutional suppression of the press.
1.2.1.4.6.1.1. Pro: It should be the people's responsibility to be skeptical and seek the truth if they feel the mainstream media is being deceptive. The word of the President is a powerful thing; he should not have abused it.
1.2.1.4.6.1.2. Con: President Trump created the [Fake News Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fake_News_Awards) in 2018 to highlight misinformation provided by news outlets.
1.2.1.4.6.2. Pro: Media news is mostly politically-driven.
1.2.1.4.6.2.1. Con: Politics are important and the news media have an integral role in "[informing marginalized segments of the population about politics](https://advances.sciencemag.org/content/6/14/eaay9344)."
1.2.1.4.6.2.2. Pro: Media coverage of Jair Bolsonaro, Brazil's current right-wing President, was in complete disregard of how his opposition [destroyed](https://foreignpolicy.com/2018/11/01/bolsonaro-cant-destroy-brazilian-democracy/) the country in the past mandates.
1.2.1.4.6.2.2.1. Con: Giving politically-driven opinions is unavoidable in any media, and \(so long as those opinions are supported by accurate and properly-represented evidence\) entirely valid. To criticise Bolsonaro is a wholly seperate matter from supporting his opposition or disregarding their failings.
1.2.1.4.6.2.2.2. Con: The second article linked says nothing about Bolsonaro's opposition destroying the country, and is itself widely critical of Bolsonaro.
1.2.1.4.6.3. Pro: The press lost the public's trust without President Trump's help. He [called out](https://www.bbc.com/news/blogs-trending-39592010) the press for being biased and was [proven correct](https://www.investors.com/politics/editorials/social-media-trump-conservative-bias/).
1.2.1.4.6.3.1. Pro: There has always been [media bias](https://www.realclearpolitics.com/articles/2013/06/12/a_brief_history_of_media_bias_118781.html) and "yellow journalism", therefore criticism is often warranted.
1.2.1.4.6.3.2. Con: The tenuous relationship between the article and the claim explained that fake news was read and shared by both the right and the left, and it didn't seem to be 'primarily an issue of the uneducated' as some believed. Mostly it was just people reading things that they already supported and passing them on.
1.2.1.4.6.3.2.1. Pro: The supporting source makes a mention of facts whose meaning is subject to interpretation, but the article makes no attempt to offer alternative interpretations.
1.2.1.4.6.3.2.1.1. Pro: People working for Amazon give 90% of their donations to left leaning candidates, and 10% to right leaning candidates. The article implies this causes them to manipulate data towards the left. But they could be examining the data and moving to the left because of it.
1.2.1.4.6.3.2.2. Pro: The article claimed that "put another way, socialist presidential candidate Bernie Sanders raked in nearly half again as much as both Republican presidential nominees. So claims that the social media giants are politically neutral were a joke."
1.2.1.4.6.3.2.2.1. Pro: Sanders's campaign was [structured](https://www.ibtimes.com/how-bernie-sanders-changed-democratic-fundraising-beating-hillary-clintons-total-2379240) to encourage small donations from people so he didn't have to take money from [PACS](https://www.opensecrets.org/pres16/candidate?id=N00000528), [unlike](https://www.opensecrets.org/pres16) the presidential nominees. The fact that more people donated to him was to be expected.
1.2.1.4.6.3.3. Con: The cited articles are about social media, not about established media. The spread of fake news via social media is a problem, but the distrust of established media sources is partially due to the conflation of those sources with things that are seen on social media.
1.2.1.4.6.3.3.1. Pro: It is the equivalent of saying that it's CNN's own fault that people don't trust it, because of the articles it published in the National Enquirer.
1.2.2. Con: President Trump authorized the use of tear gas and rubber bullets on [peaceful protesters](https://www.poynter.org/newsletters/2020/peaceful-protesters-were-attacked-as-trump-spoke-and-the-media-thankfully-was-there-to-shine-a-light-on-it/) fighting for justice for George Floyd on the 1st of June 2020.
1.2.3. Pro: An [executive order](https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2020/06/02/2020-12030/preventing-online-censorship)(Executive Order 13925 of May 28, 2020\n\nPreventing Online Censorship\n\nBy the authority vested in me as President by the Constitution and the laws of the United States of America, it is hereby ordered as follows:) on preventing online censorship was released in May 2020.
1.2.3.1. Pro: President Trump stated his willingness to prevent the [online censorship of Twitter](https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2020/06/02/2020-12030/preventing-online-censorship)(Twitter, Facebook, Instagram, and YouTube wield immense, if not unprecedented, power to shape the interpretation of public events; to censor, delete, or disappear information; and to control what people see or do not see.\n\nAs President, I have made clear my commitment to free and open debate on the internet. Such debate is just as important online as it is in our universities, our town halls, and our homes. It is essential to sustaining our democracy.) as the platform had a tendency to selectively "place a warning label on certain tweets in a manner that clearly reflected political bias."
1.2.3.2. Con: An order to prevent private companies from reducing the spread of misinformation is not a measure to protect "free speech" but a license to lie.
1.2.4. Con: President Trump severely [damaged the exercise of free speech](https://www.politifact.com/personalities/donald-trump/).
1.2.4.1. Pro: These concerns about "free speech" often seem to focus more on [protecting certain groups from any criticism](https://www.newyorker.com/news/news-desk/race-and-the-free-speech-diversion) rather than protecting the right broadly for all groups, in all cases.
1.2.4.2. Pro: President Trump's abuse of free speech [left America more vulnerable to disasters](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/fixgov/2020/05/01/destroying-trust-in-the-media-science-and-government-has-left-america-vulnerable-to-disaster/).
1.2.5. Con: President Trump used the [rhetoric of hate](https://www.shs-conferences.org/articles/shsconf/pdf/2019/13/shsconf_appsconf2019_03038.pdf) during his presidency.
1.2.5.1. Pro: Much of the freedom President Trump advocated for opened the way for hate speech, racism, and toxic discourse.
1.2.5.1.1. Pro: President Trump's senior campaign advisor and speechwriter used coded messages that referenced and allied with [white supremacy](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/security/reports/2020/07/01/482414/white-supremacy-returned-mainstream-politics/), as shown by his leaked emails.
1.2.5.1.2. Pro: President Trump called COVID-19 the ["Chinese virus" and "Kung flu."](https://www.usatoday.com/videos/news/nation/2020/06/22/wh-defends-trumps-use-kung-flu-rally/3238385001/)
1.2.5.1.3. Con: President Trump was honest in his fight against "[political correctness](https://www.npr.org/sections/codeswitch/2016/12/14/505324427/politically-correct-the-phrase-has-gone-from-wisdom-to-weapon)".
1.2.5.1.4. Con: The problem wasn't that President Trump advocated for freedom, but that there were elements in society that misused it.
1.2.5.2. Con: Truly free speech allows people to openly voice any kind of opinion.
1.2.5.2.1. Con: Free speech doesn't prohibit the consequences of abusing it.
1.2.5.2.2. Con: According to the [First Amendment](https://www.uscourts.gov/about-federal-courts/educational-resources/about-educational-outreach/activity-resources/what-does), freedom of speech doesn't include inciting "actions that would harm others."
1.2.5.2.3. Pro: Prohibiting specific opinions could lead to [censorship](https://www.mtsu.edu/first-amendment/article/896/censorship).
1.2.5.3. Pro: President Trump [weaponized free speech](https://www.cjr.org/the_media_today/trump_shooting_looting_facebook_zuckerberg.php).
1.2.6. Pro: President Trump issued an executive order to [protect campus free speech](https://www.acenet.edu/News-Room/Pages/President-Trump-Issues-Executive-Order-on-Campus-Free-Speech.aspx) in March 2019.
1.2.6.1. Con: The order [didn't actually protect free speech](https://theconversation.com/what-president-trumps-executive-order-on-campus-free-speech-is-really-meant-to-do-114059), instead, it gave the order to the Department of Education to provide more "granular information about student debt and earnings on [the College Scorecard](https://collegescorecard.ed.gov/)."
1.2.6.2. Pro: The aim of this order was to [improve transparency on college campuses](https://edition.cnn.com/2019/03/21/politics/campus-free-speech-executive-order-donald-trump/index.html)(Trump: If college won't let you speak, we won't give money.) by promoting free speech.
1.2.7. Pro: On May 4, 2017, President Trump signed the executive order "[Promoting Free Speech and Religious Liberty](https://www.state.gov/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/DoS-Implementation-of-Executive-Order-13798-508.pdf)" which gave greater freedom in political speech to religious organizations.
1.2.7.1. Pro: This executive order aimed at relaxing [political restrictions on religious groups of all denominations](https://www.npr.org/2017/05/04/526840823/annotated-trumps-executive-order-on-religious-liberty).
1.2.7.1.1. Pro: The executive order protected different entities by providing approximately [13.7 million people with health care and other social services](https://www.frc.org/executiveorder).
1.2.7.1.2. Con: The executive order licensed discrimination by using "[religious liberty to justify discrimination](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/lgbtq-rights/news/2017/07/31/436871/religious-liberty-executive-order-licenses-discrimination/)".
1.2.7.2. Con: The executive order gave more [freedom to churches in order to strenghen birth control restrictions](http://pulse.ncpolicywatch.org/2017/05/04/trumps-new-order-political-freedom-churches-religion-back-table-deny-birth-control/).
1.2.7.2.1. Pro: This executive order was criticized for "[hurting women](https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/trump-signs-religious-liberty-executive-order-allowing-broad-exemptions-n754786)("Plain and simple: President Trump’s executive order will hurt women," Nancy Northup, president and CEO of the Center for Reproductive Rights said in a statement. "And the Center for Reproductive Rights is ready to fight back in court.)".
1.2.7.2.2. Con: The executive order was signed with the idea of [defending the freedom of religion and speech in America](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/trump-signs-religious-liberty-order-to-defend-freedom-of-religion/).
1.3. Con: President Trump committed many [immoral actions](https://theintercept.com/2019/12/19/a-z-trump-impeachment/) - the character of a leader is of utmost importance.
1.3.1. Pro: President Trump's personal and professional lives were littered with a number of [serious moral failings](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2018/01/15/opinion/leonhardt-trump-racist.html) long before he became President.

Pro: At least 26 women have [accused](https://www.businessinsider.com/women-accused-trump-sexual-misconduct-list-2017-12)("A deluge of women made their accusations public following the October 2016 publication of the "Access Hollywood" tape, in which Trump was heard boasting about grabbing women's genitals in 2005.") President Trump of sexually harassing or assaulting them.

Pro: A book called "[All the President's Women: Donald Trump and the making of a predator](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/trump-sexual-assault-allegations-all-list-misconduct-karen-johnson-how-many-a9149216.html)" detailed full 26 incidents of “unwanted sexual contact” and 43 instances of inappropriate behavior.

Pro: According to [The Guardian](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2020/sep/17/amy-dorris-donald-trump-women-who-accuse-sexual-misconduct)(The list of women who have publicly made sexual misconduct allegations against Donald Trump outnumbers the list of officials in his cabinet. 1.3.8.1.1.2. Con: The fact that his associates committed crimes doesn't prove that President Trump participated in those crimes.
1.3.8.1.1.2.1. Con: It does, however, raise questions about President Trump's possible knowledge of and deliberate ignorance of these crimes.
1.3.8.1.2. Con: It is unlikely that a US President can [face criminal prosecution in court](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-trump-russia-indictment-explainer/can-a-sitting-us-president-face-criminal-charges-idUSKCN1QF1D3).
1.3.8.2. Pro: Revelations published in January 2021, show that President Trump engaged in a [criminal conspiracy](https://www.justsecurity.org/66271/timeline-trump-giuliani-bidens-and-ukrainegate/).
1.3.8.2.1. Pro: President Trump also engaged in a coverup of that conspiracy, to smear his [political opponent Joe Biden in 2019](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump%E2%80%93Ukraine_scandal)(A political scandal in the United States involving efforts by U.S. President Donald Trump to coerce Ukraine and other foreign countries into providing damaging narratives about the 2020 Democratic Party presidential candidate Joe Biden as well as misinformation relating to Russian interference in the 2016 United States elections.).
1.3.8.2.1.1. Pro: This was done by extorting the government of Ukraine through illegally [withholding](https://www.washingtonpost.com/national-security/trump-ordered-hold-on-military-aid-days-before-calling-ukrainian-president-officials-say/2019/09/23/df93a6ca-de38-11e9-8dc8-498eabc129a0_story.html) congressionally approved aid unless President Trump's demands were met.
1.3.8.2.1.2. Con: President Trump stated that he [only discussed political rival Joe Biden with the president of Ukraine](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/2020-election/there-s-no-evidence-trump-s-biden-ukraine-accusations-what-n1057851)(President Donald Trump says he discussed political rival Joe Biden with the president of Ukraine — a phone call reportedly at the heart of a whistleblower complaint that has led to the launch of formal impeachment proceedings in the House — for one reason: a desire to root out corruption.) during a phone call.
1.3.8.2.2. Con: President Trump was [acquitted by the Senate](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-51394383) following the impeachment on charges of abusing the power of his office and obstructing Congress.
1.3.8.3. Pro: President Trump was involved in the [obstruction of justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obstruction_of_justice)(Obstruction of justice, in United States jurisdictions, is a crime consisting of obstructing prosecutors, investigators, or other government officials. Common law jurisdictions other than the United States tend to use the wider offense of perverting the course of justice.), as described in the [Muller Report](https://www.justice.gov/storage/report.pdf)(Report On The Investigation Into Russian Interference In The 2016 Presidential Election.) submitted in March 2019.
1.3.8.3.1. Pro: The report included allegations of conspiracy and coordination between [President Trump and Russia](https://www.seattletimes.com/opinion/18-reasons-trump-could-be-a-russian-asset/)(In the days after President Donald Trump fired James Comey as F.B.I. director, law enforcement officials became so concerned by the president’s behavior that they began investigating whether he had been working on behalf of Russia against American interests.).
1.3.8.3.1.1. Pro: The Moscow Project analyzed and found a long history of [business deals between President Trump and Putin](https://themoscowproject.org/)(How decades of Donald Trump's business dealings and Vladimir Putin's assault on Western democracy converged during the 2016 election cycle and beyond.).
1.3.8.3.1.1.1. Con: President Trump was a businessman dealing with many countries. Business deals with a country are not suspicious.
1.3.8.3.1.1.2. Con: The [Moscow Project](https://themoscowproject.org/) is an aggressively anti-Trump group.
1.3.8.3.1.2. Con: The FBI concluded that there was no [clear connection between President Trump and Russia](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-47688187).
1.3.8.3.2. Pro: Robert Muller’s [investigation](https://www.acslaw.org/projects/the-presidential-investigation-education-project/other-resources/key-findings-of-the-mueller-report/)(The investigation produced 37 indictments; seven guilty pleas or convictions; and compelling evidence that the president obstructed justice on multiple occasions.) identified 10 instances of possible obstruction of justice.
1.3.8.3.2.1. Pro: In March 2019, the investigation resulted in [dozens of indictments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Counsel_investigation_\(2017%E2%80%932019\)) for federal crimes, and at least eight guilty pleas, or convictions.
1.3.8.3.2.2. Pro: More than [1000 former federal prosecutors](https://medium.com/\@dojalumni/statement-by-former-federal-prosecutors-8ab7691c2aa1)(Each of us believes that the conduct of President Trump described in Special Counsel Robert Mueller’s report would, in the case of any other person not covered by the Office of Legal Counsel policy against indicting a sitting President, result in multiple felony charges for obstruction of justice.) agreed that President Trump’s conduct, had he had been a private citizen, would have resulted in multiple felony charges.
1.3.8.3.3. Con: President Trump called the Muller report the “[greatest Political Crime in the History of the U.S., the Russian Witch-Hunt](https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2020/07/06/why-the-mueller-investigation-failed).”
1.3.8.3.4. Con: The Muller report didn't find [enough evidence of the link between President Trump and Russia](https://www.americanbar.org/news/abanews/aba-news-archives/2019/03/mueller-concludes-investigation/)(Special counsel Robert Mueller’s investigation did not find sufficient evidence that President Donald Trump’s campaign coordinated with Russia to influence the United States’ 2016 election and did not take a clear position on whether Trump obstructed justice.), and left the question of obstruction of justice open.
1.3.8.4. Pro: President Trump has been involved in various financial crimes.
1.3.8.4.1. Pro: President Trump paid [$25 million](https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/white-house/federal-court-approves-25-million-trump-university-settlement-n845181) to settle with students he defrauded at the now-defunct Trump University.
1.3.8.4.2. Pro: [President Trump paid $2 million in fines for misusing charity funds.](https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2019/12/10/donald-trump-pays-2-million-charity-foundation-saga/4387949002/)
1.3.8.4.3. Con: Even if President Trump might have been involved in financial crimes, as President of the United States, he had [protection from legal action](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-54716550), and therefore the crimes weren't proven.
1.3.8.4.4. Pro: President Trump was in violation of the [Constitution's foreign emoluments clause](https://www.britannica.com/story/what-is-the-emoluments-clause)(A provision of the U.S. Constitution \(Article I, Section 9, Paragraph 8\) that generally prohibits federal officeholders from receiving any gift, payment, or other thing of value from a foreign state or its rulers, officers, or representatives.) and earned [countless foreign revenue](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2017/mar/08/china-approves-trump-trademarks-businesses) for his and his family's businesses.
1.3.8.4.4.1. Con: Generating revenue by your business is not considered a gift, emolument, office, or title from foreign states, therefore it was not in violation of the [Title of Nobility Clause](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Title_of_Nobility_Clause)(The Titles of Nobility Clause was designed to shield the federal officeholders of the United States against so-called "corrupting foreign influences.).
1.3.8.4.4.1.1. Con: Simply generating revenue is not the issue. It is the [revenue received due in part to being U.S. President which afforded foreign countries a favor.](https://www.salon.com/2018/12/07/veterans-say-the-saudi-regime-duped-them-to-funnel-funds-to-the-presidents-business-empire_partner/)
1.3.8.4.4.2. Pro: President Trump [profited off the Presidency](https://www.acslaw.org/expertforum/profiting-off-the-presidency-trumps-violations-of-the-emoluments-clauses/)(President Donald Trump has been violating the Constitution since noon on January 20, 2017.), which was a violation of the Emoluments Clauses.
1.3.8.4.4.3. Pro: In respect to the emoluments clause, President Trump unconstitutionally [accepted payments from foreign and domestic governments](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2018/12/17/us/politics/trump-emoluments-money.html?mtrref=www.usatoday.com&assetType=REGIWALL).
1.3.8.5. Con: If being implicated in crimes disqualified someone from being president, the American people would be left with very few good candidates.
1.4. Pro: President Trump improved the United States during his presidency.
1.4.1. Pro: President Trump has [helped the U.S. economy](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-45827430).
1.4.1.1. Con: President Trump's [weak public health and economic response](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/economy/news/2020/06/03/485806/5-ways-trump-administrations-policy-failures-compounded-coronavirus-induced-economic-crisis/) to the pandemic caused great financial harm to the country.
1.4.1.1.1. Con: COVID-19 created a [recession in the global economy](https://www.worldbank.org/en/news/press-release/2020/06/08/covid-19-to-plunge-global-economy-into-worst-recession-since-world-war-ii), independently of President Trump's weak responses.
1.4.1.1.1.1. Con: The United States' economy powers the world economy due to its unmatched size.
1.4.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: The United States spends [trillions of dollars](https://www.statista.com/statistics/252246/total-value-of-us-international-trade/) anually in global international trade.
1.4.1.1.2. Pro: President Trump’s loose fiscal policy before the pandemic left America with much higher debt when entering into the [crisis](https://www.economist.com/united-states/2020/10/14/how-the-american-economy-did-under-donald-trump).
1.4.1.2. Pro: President Trump enacted [corporate tax reform](https://www.investopedia.com/taxes/trumps-tax-reform-plan-explained/).
1.4.1.2.1. Con: President Trump said his tax policies would result in much faster growth, as high as 6%. GDP [grew](https://www.bea.gov/news/glance) 2.4% in 2017, 2.9% in 2018 and through the 3rd quarter of 2019, average growth was just 2.3%.
1.4.1.2.2. Pro: President Trump promised to lower the [corporate tax rate](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-37982000), and he brought corporation tax down from 35% to 15%.
1.4.1.2.2.1. Con: In terms of the [economy and the deficit](https://www.investopedia.com/articles/07/tax_cuts.asp), this may prove to be a bad move in the long run.
1.4.1.2.2.2. Con: This meant [billions](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/economy/news/2019/09/26/475083/trumps-corporate-tax-cut-not-trickling/) of dollars in lost revenues and was not a fiscally responsible decision.
1.4.1.2.2.3. Con: [Lowering the corporate tax rate](https://www.cbpp.org/under-new-tax-law-high-income-investors-can-use-corporations-to-defer-their-taxes-for-decades-1) substantially below the top personal income tax rate can jeopardize the integrity of the tax system as high-income individuals will attempt to shelter their savings within corporations.
1.4.1.2.3. Pro: The corporate tax reform was needed to allow US manufacturers to [compete](https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefings-statements/praise-president-trumps-commitment-tax-reform/) on a global stage, with [tax rates more on par with other nation's tax rates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tax_Cuts_and_Jobs_Act_of_2017).
1.4.1.2.4. Con: President Trump's tax reforms helped the [mega-rich](https://www.forbes.com/sites/camilomaldonado/2019/10/10/trump-tax-cuts-helped-billionaires-pay-less-taxes-than-the-working-class-in-2018/?sh=7e4881373128) of America get away with paying less in taxes than the working class.
1.4.1.3. Con: In November 2020, the US economy had the biggest [economic contraction](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-45827430) ever recorded and the highest unemployment rate in more than 80 years.
1.4.1.3.1. Pro: The national debt soared to almost [$23 trillion](https://usdebtclock.org/) and the total debt over $74 trillion under his presidency.
1.4.1.3.2. Pro: The [US unemployment rate](https://economictimes.indiatimes.com/news/international/business/us-economy-doing-amazingly-well-trump/articleshow/76490224.cms?from=mdr) for April 2020 was 14.7%, which was the highest since 1948.
1.4.1.3.2.1. Pro: An estimated 300,000 US jobs were lost because of [President Trump's trade war with China](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/trumps-trade-war-squashed-an-estimated-300000-jobs-so-far-moodys-estimates/).
1.4.1.3.2.2. Con: The US unemployment rate for [February 2020 was 3.5%](https://www.bls.gov/charts/employment-situation/civilian-unemployment-rate.htm) according to the Bureau of Labor Statistics. Conflating unemployment because of the pandemic with unemployment as a product of President Trump's economy is a fallacy. [Since April 2020, it has dropped to 7.9%](https://www.bls.gov/charts/employment-situation/civilian-unemployment-rate.htm).
1.4.1.3.3. Con: The "economic contraction" was a product of the COVID-19 pandemic, not a product of Trump's economic policies. Before the pandemic hit, the [US unemployment rate was 3.5%](https://www.bls.gov/charts/employment-situation/civilian-unemployment-rate.htm), the lowest in the last two decades.
1.4.1.3.3.1. Con: The economy cannot prosper if the President fails to address threats to national security. Policies that outwardly are not economic in nature are linked to the economy.
1.4.1.4. Con: President Trump didn't help the US economy. He [inherited a strong economy from Obama's administration](https://www.jec.senate.gov/public/_cache/files/2c298bda-8aee-4923-84a3-95a54f7f6e6f/did-trump-create-or-inherit-the-strong-economy.pdf).
1.4.1.5. Pro: President Trump's stewardship and policies led to historic economic achievements across a number of different metrics.
1.4.1.5.1. Con: President Trump's stewardship or service to anything that didn't directly or indirectly [benefit himself, or his legacy](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/democracy/reports/2017/04/27/431387/trump-100-days-case-studies-trumps-self-serving-special-interest-government/), was non-existent.
1.4.1.5.2. Con: The economy was strong [as a result of President Obama's economic decision](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/09/09/us/politics/trump-obama-economy.html). Most of President Trump's decisions only had a [negligible or net negative effect](https://www.cnbc.com/2019/02/28/trumps-economic-policies-failed-to-deliver-promised-3percent-growth-in-2018.html) on the economy.
1.4.1.5.2.1. Con: Under Trump's administration, [the median household income grew from $62,898 in 2016 to $68,703 in 2019](https://theprint.in/opinion/donald-trumps-economy-really-was-better-than-obamas/534326/).
1.4.1.5.2.2. Pro: [Analysts](https://fivethirtyeight.com/features/a-presidents-economic-decisions-matter-eventually/) and [economists](http://fortune.com/2017/07/20/donald-trump-economy-stock-market-jobs-reports-credit/) argue that it takes two or more years for presidential decisions to have a noticeable effect on the economy, outside of crisis situations.
1.4.1.5.2.2.1. Con: White House economist Kevin Hassett stated that President Trump deserved all the credit for the U.S. [economic 'inflection](https://www.npr.org/2018/09/12/646708799/fact-check-who-gets-credit-for-the-booming-u-s-economy)'.
1.4.1.5.2.2.2. Pro: This implies that the results can be attributed to Obama, not to President Trump.
1.4.1.5.3. Pro: He pushed through a [revolutionary tax reform](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/27/us/politics/trump-tax-cut-plan-middle-class-deficit.html).
1.4.1.5.3.1. Pro: President Trump's tax reforms [stretched](https://www.investopedia.com/taxes/trumps-tax-reform-plan-explained/) tax brackets and reduced taxes on the middle class.
1.4.1.5.3.1.1. Pro: The Tax Cuts and Jobs Act \(TCJA\) reduced "[statutory tax rates at almost all levels of taxable income](https://www.taxpolicycenter.org/briefing-book/how-did-tax-cuts-and-jobs-act-change-personal-taxes)," together with a shift in the thresholds for several income tax brackets.
1.4.1.5.3.1.2. Con: Individual and family taxes will expire in 2025, while the law created a permanent [single corporate tax rate of 21%](https://www.investopedia.com/taxes/trumps-tax-reform-plan-explained/).
1.4.1.5.3.2. Pro: The Tax Cuts and Jobs Act was considered the [largest overhaul of the tax code in three decades](https://taxfoundation.org/tax-reform-explained-tax-cuts-and-jobs-act/).
1.4.1.5.3.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.4.1.5.3.1.1.
1.4.1.5.3.3. Con: The Tax Reform was of undetermined value - although 37/38 economists thought it was terrible, and the 38th [misread the question](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2017/11/22/37-of-38-economists-said-the-gop-tax-plans-would-grow-the-debt-the-38th-misread-the-question/?noredirect=on&utm_term=.e00556927769).
1.4.1.5.3.3.1. Pro: It was vital to canvass opinions from [experts in the field](http://www.igmchicago.org/surveys/tax-reform-2), given that President Trump was not an economist and [every new measure](https://www.economist.com/democracy-in-america/2017/12/02/the-senate-passes-a-tax-bill?zid=297&ah=3ae0fe266c7447d8a0c7ade5547d62ca) seemed likely to worsen America's financial situation.
1.4.1.5.3.3.2. Con: The [economy was booming](https://www.independent.co.uk/voices/trade-war-tariffs-us-economy-jobs-report-federal-reserve-g7-finance-ministers-wilbur-ross-china-a8380631.html) after the tax cut legislation, suggesting that these economists have zero predictive power.
1.4.1.5.3.4. Con: The tax cut boosted the [Federal deficit to trillion-dollars](https://www.usatoday.com/story/opinion/2018/08/20/donald-trump-trillion-dollar-plus-deficits-fiscal-ruin-column/986236002/), on top of the already high deficits imposed by the previous administration to counter the 2008 financial crash and recession.
1.4.1.5.3.5. Pro: There are additional benefits to people that may flow from longer-term macroeconomic factors, commonly known as '[trickle-down](https://www.thebalance.com/trickle-down-economics-theory-effect-does-it-work-3305572)(Trickle-down economics is a theory that claims benefits for the wealthy trickle down to everyone else. These benefits are tax cuts on businesses, high-income earners, capital gains, and dividends.)' economics.
1.4.1.5.3.5.1. Con: The long-term effects of the tax cut were already [costing the US $2.3 trillion](https://www.politico.com/story/2018/02/28/tax-cuts-trump-gop-analysis-430781) in 2018.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2. Con: Ample [research](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/jan/20/trickle-down-economics-broken-promise-richest-85) and [examples](https://www.thebalance.com/trickle-down-economics-theory-effect-does-it-work-3305572) have [shown](http://www.chicagotribune.com/news/opinion/letters/ct-trickle-down-economics-doesn-t-work-20171124-story.html) that trickle down economics do not often [work](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2017-11-30/the-best-way-to-spur-growth-help-the-poor-not-the-rich) as intended.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1. Con: The [economy was booming](https://www.independent.co.uk/voices/trade-war-tariffs-us-economy-jobs-report-federal-reserve-g7-finance-ministers-wilbur-ross-china-a8380631.html) in 2018, suggesting all of those sources are irrelevant.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.1. Pro: The U.S. economy grew [2.9% In 2018](https://www.npr.org/2019/02/28/698884578/u-s-economy-grew-2-9-percent-in-2018-just-below-trumps-target).
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.2. Pro: The [equity market performance](http://www.uobgroup.com.sg/web-resources/uobgroup/pdf/research/MN_201028B.pdf?adobe_mc=MCMID%3D58807668847636526022661862915996130797%7CMCORGID%3D116168F454E6DA2A0A4C98A6%2540AdobeOrg%7CTS%3D1604361601) was considerably better during President Trump's first three years, compared to the same period for President Obama. \(p.5\)
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.3. Con: Particular parts of the economy were "booming". But [growing household debt](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-fed-debt-charts-graphic-idUSKBN1XN2OH), and [growing income inequality](https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2019/09/26/income-inequality-america-highest-its-been-since-census-started-tracking-it-data-show/), combined with growing [cost of living](https://www.bls.gov/charts/consumer-price-index/consumer-price-index-by-category-line-chart.htm) is NOT a good kind of "boom".
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.4. Con: This is a [post hoc ergo propter hoc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post_hoc_ergo_propter_hoc) fallacy. Simply because there have been positive economic occurrences during the Trump presidency does not mean that he caused them.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.4.1. Pro: Many of the [metrics](https://www.economicshelp.org/blog/25420/economics/us-economy-under-obama-2009-2017/) are the same as 2019 being the biggest year on record. All economic metrics continued the same trend that were in place from his predecessor. Except the Dow, which was negative in 2018 after huge growth.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.4.2. Pro: [Evidence shows](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2018/8/24/17759940/donald-trump-economy-jobs-growth-obama) these economic occurrences to be a continuation of [long-term trends](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/article/2018/jul/27/fact-checking-donald-trumps-points-about-economy/) that pre-date him.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.4.3. Pro: Under Hitler, Nazi Germany experienced a massive revival and uplift in its [economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Nazi_Germany#Recovery_and_rearmament). This did not make him a good leader. By the same metric, these didn't make Trump a good President.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.4.3.1. Con: Hitler's economic advancements were not what made him a bad leader, but the [genocide of millions of people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Holocaust) and the stain he created on Germany. As horrible as Hitler was, it is possible for him to have done deeds that in themselves were good. A definition of [good](https://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/good) can be `benefit or advantage to someone or something.` Therefore, we should compare the actions that were advantageous against actions that were disadvantageous.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.5. Con: The 2018 upward trend in the economy and employment was already a [reality before President Trump took office](https://www.npr.org/2018/09/12/646708799/fact-check-who-gets-credit-for-the-booming-u-s-economy).
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.5.1. Pro: This was in spite of President Trump, [not because of him](http://theweek.com/articles/786614/americas-economy-booming-trump-nothing). It was growing along the [same basic trajectory](https://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/plum-line/wp/2018/01/26/that-trump-economic-boom-its-mostly-hype/) as before he took office.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.5.2. Con: Median [family income](https://www.bloombergquint.com/gadfly/trump-s-economy-really-was-better-than-obama-s) soared under President Trump's administration.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.5.3. Con: The average hourly earnings rose at [3% per month, on average, compared to 2.3%](http://www.uobgroup.com.sg/web-resources/uobgroup/pdf/research/MN_201028B.pdf?adobe_mc=MCMID%3D58807668847636526022661862915996130797%7CMCORGID%3D116168F454E6DA2A0A4C98A6%2540AdobeOrg%7CTS%3D1604361601) under Obama's administration. \(p. 3\)
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.1.5.4. Pro: -> See 1.4.1.5.2.2.
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.2. Pro: The theory of trickle-down economics [doesn't work](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/jan/20/trickle-down-economics-broken-promise-richest-85), as cutting the top tax rate does [not lead to economic growth](http://www.faireconomy.org/trickle_down_economics_four_reasons).
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.3. Pro: Supply-side economics result in greater [income inequality](https://www.cbo.gov/publication/42729).
1.4.1.5.3.5.2.4. Pro: The rise of national and local [costs of living](https://www.investopedia.com/ask/answers/101314/what-does-current-cost-living-compare-20-years-ago.asp) as well as natural currency [inflation](http://www.faireconomy.org/trickle_down_economics_four_reasons) increases at a faster and steeper [rate](https://www.statista.com/statistics/244983/projected-inflation-rate-in-the-united-states/) than the rate at which funds can [trickle](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2017-11-30/the-best-way-to-spur-growth-help-the-poor-not-the-rich) from higher socio-economic levels to lower ones.
1.4.1.5.3.5.3. Pro: According to the [trickle-down theory](https://www.economicshelp.org/blog/174/economics/trickle-down-economics/), if the richest increase their wealth, they will spend a proportion of this extra wealth, which will cause more demand for goods and services and higher employment.
1.4.1.5.3.6. Con: The tax cuts [primarily benefit](https://www.bloomberg.com/graphics/2018-tax-plan-consequences/) the owners of capital via the businesses they own. In total dollar terms, only a marginal portion of the tax cuts benefited the so-called ‘hard-working Americans’.
1.4.1.5.3.7. Pro: The executive branch with President Trump at the helm was [slashing bloated regulations](https://www.americanactionforum.org/insight/two-months-to-go-regulatory-budget-progress/). At the last count for the financial year of 2018, 47 regulations were cut & 10 new regulations were created, resulting in YTD savings of $621.5M in taxpayer money.
1.4.1.5.3.7.1. Con: It is still very unclear if this was a good thing or not. The overall savings weren't very high at $8 billion, while the cost was harder to quantify as some of the deregulatory actions and the blocking of new regulations may have put lives in jeopardy as a [result.](https://www.politico.com/agenda/story/2018/01/20/trumps-regulatory-experiment-year-one-000620)
1.4.1.5.4. Con: Overall, [President Trump's economic policies increased economic inequality](https://www.cbo.gov/publication/55941).
1.4.1.5.5. Pro: The American economy was experiencing [4.2%](https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-gdp-growth-revised-up-in-second-quarter-1535546347) GDP growth in 2018, which contrasted positively against the recession [predicted](http://robertreich.org/post/136616314155) by some economists.
1.4.1.5.5.1. Con: The economy has been [booming](https://data.bls.gov/timeseries/LNS14000000) since 2010, while the tax plan was passed at the end of [2017](https://www.statista.com/statistics/188165/annual-gdp-growth-of-the-united-states-since-1990/). The inflation, however, [accelerated](https://www.thebalance.com/unemployment-rate-by-year-3305506) since Trump became President.
1.4.1.5.5.2. Pro: -> See 1.4.1.5.3.3.2.
1.4.1.5.6. Pro: U.S. small business optimism hit its [highest level in history](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2018-09-11/u-s-small-business-optimism-at-record-high-on-hiring-spending) under Trump's presidency.
1.4.1.5.6.1. Con: That is not proof of any policy success. The index is provided by the [NFIB](https://www.sourcewatch.org/index.php/National_Federation_of_Independent_Business), which surveys only a small fraction of its members, which represent only about 10% \(300k of 30 million\) of small businesses in the nation, and is backed by and lobbies for large corporate interests.
1.4.1.5.6.2. Pro: Consumer confidence surged to an [18 year high](https://www.theguardian.com/business/2018/aug/29/us-economy-second-quarter-revised-report-figures) in 2018.
1.4.1.5.6.2.1. Con: The article cited is two years old. Because of President Trump's failure, [millions of Americans](https://www.marketwatch.com/story/new-us-jobless-claims-flat-at-884000-a-fresh-wave-of-layoffs-hitting-the-economy-2020-09-10?mod=article_inline) are still out of work, and others [anticipate losing their homes](https://www.aspeninstitute.org/blog-posts/the-covid-19-eviction-crisis-an-estimated-30-40-million-people-in-america-are-at-risk/). In light of this, consumer confidence considerably reduced, and is [likely to stay that way](https://www.marketwatch.com/story/there-will-be-no-v-shaped-recovery-for-consumer-sentiment-datatrek-says-2020-08-18) for a while.
1.4.1.5.6.3. Pro: America’s biggest companies [reported](https://fortune.com/2019/11/05/corporate-earnings-markets-up-recession/) some of the strongest earnings growth since the recession under Trump's presidency.
1.4.1.5.7. Pro: The USA experienced historically low unemployment under President Trump.
1.4.1.5.7.1. Con: The trend was [present in the previous administration as well.](https://www.forbes.com/sites/chuckjones/2020/07/04/trumps-unemployment-rates-are-still-worse-than-obamas-highest-numbers/) There is no reason to believe that President Trump's policies had anything to do with it.
1.4.1.5.7.1.1. Con: President Trump created 6.6 million jobs in his first three years, which was a [4.4% increase](https://www.thebalance.com/job-creation-by-president-by-number-and-percent-3863218) compared to the end of Obama's term.
1.4.1.5.7.1.2. Pro: [This chart](https://data.bls.gov/timeseries/LNS14000000) shows what the unemployment numbers actually are. They have fallen about one percentage point each year since 2011, this trend was continuing until COVID-19.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3. Pro: Economic indicators do not necessarily prove when a President is doing well. The suggestion that a President can directly control and manipulate the American economy and is entirely responsible for its success or failure is absurd.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.1. Pro: President Obama entered office during the [economic crisis](https://www.brookings.edu/research/president-barack-obamas-first-two-years-policy-accomplishments-political-difficulties/) and throughout the majority of his first year was dealing with large unemployment. This didn't mean that he was an unsuccessful President.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.2. Con: Certain indicators like the incentive to be reelected result in an [increase in presidential effort on GDP growth](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/264087748_Can_the_president_really_affect_economic_growth_Presidential_effort_and_the_political_business_cycle).
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.2.1. Con: Economic arguments for the success of a president are based as much on [partisanship as they are on data](https://www.forbes.com/sites/realspin/2016/11/07/trump-is-right-about-one-thing-the-economy-does-better-under-the-democrats/#51245ee86786).
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.3. Pro: The President's claim of job creation as evidence of his success was overstated. Job growth continued on the trend in [Obama's second term](https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/2019/08/20/trump-v-obama-economy-charts/), albeit at a slower pace.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.3.1. Pro: According to the [Bureau of Labor Statistics](https://data.bls.gov/timeseries/CES0000000001?output_view=net_1mth), job growth in 2017 was lower than past four years.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.3.1.1. Pro: 2018's growth of 208k jobs \(through Sept\), was lower than 2015 and 2016. If the President's claim was that his tax cuts created jobs, it was not evident in job numbers.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.3.2. Con: Job creation under President Trump's administration [started stronger than President Obama's](https://fortune.com/longform/comparing-trump-on-jobs-us-economy-past-presidents-obama-bush-clinton/), until it was hit by COVID-19.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.3.3. Pro: Unemployment rates were at [record lows](http://www.oecd.org/economy/labour/47656668.pdf) in many other countries as a result of a long global expansion that followed the financial crisis in 2008.
1.4.1.5.7.1.3.3.3.1. Pro: Many of these countries had policies directly contrary to the President's. Thirty-six countries had rates lower than the USA, including Japan \(2.4%\), Germany \(3.4%\), Mexico \(3.4%\), Poland \(3.5%\), and Hungary \(3.6%\).
1.4.1.5.7.2. Pro: Black and [Hispanic](https://www.cnsnews.com/news/article/craig-bannister/hispanic-latino-unemployment-rate-hits-lowest-level-record-june) unemployment rates were [historically low](https://www.marketwatch.com/story/black-unemployment-falls-to-second-lowest-on-record-2018-09-07) in 2018 and 2019.
1.4.1.5.7.2.1. Con: This is more a result of [Obama's policies than Trump's](https://www.factcheck.org/2018/01/trump-takes-undue-credit-black-unemployment/).
1.4.1.5.7.2.2. Pro: In September 2019, Black unemployment hit the [record rate of 5.5%](https://www.cnbc.com/2019/10/04/black-and-hispanic-unemployment-is-at-a-record-low.html).
1.4.1.5.7.3. Pro: Female unemployment was at the [lowest rate for 65 years](https://www.newsweek.com/trump-female-employment-sorry-women-i-let-you-down-again-1098500) in 2018.
1.4.1.5.7.3.1. Pro: The unemployment rate for women fell to [3.6%](https://www.dol.gov/newsroom/releases/osec/osec20181005).
1.4.1.5.7.3.2. Con: Even if 863,000 women joined the workforce during the first 11 months of Trump's presidency, that number still represented [34% less](https://www.factcheck.org/2018/01/misleading-talking-point-women-workers/) when compared to the same period, from January to December, in each of the last two years.
1.4.1.5.7.4. Con: Even assuming that [lower unemployment was a result of President Trump's](https://www.businessinsider.com/obama-trump-gop-economy-job-growth-report-2018-9) actions during his time in office, [wealth inequality](https://newrepublic.com/minutes/151188/growing-inequality-trump-era) was [increasing](https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-economic-agenda-is-exacerbating-americas-inequality-crisis-2018-8), and [wages](https://www.forbes.com/sites/eriksherman/2016/11/12/what-a-trump-administration-might-mean-for-income-inequality/#18f88433a783) when adjusted for inflation were stagnant.
1.4.1.5.7.4.1. Pro: It is also important to take into account whether the new jobs created provided [liveable wages](https://undocs.org/A/HRC/38/33/ADD.1). A stronger economy ought to mean real benefits for average families, not just those at the top.
1.4.1.5.7.5. Pro: In 2018, the unemployment rate was at its [lowest in 50 years](https://www.npr.org/2018/10/05/654417887/u-s-unemployment-rate-drops-to-3-7-percent-lowest-in-nearly-50-years), when it dropped to 3.7%.
1.4.1.5.7.5.1. Con: The trend towards low [unemployment](https://tradingeconomics.com/united-states/unemployment-rate) has been following a relatively unchanged curve for 10 years \(far longer than Trump's presidency\), and if anything, that curve only shallowed since President Trump took office.
1.4.1.5.7.5.2. Pro: After the 2020 increase due to COVID-19, the [rate of unemployment dropped from 14.7% \(April\) to 13.3%](https://edition.cnn.com/2020/06/05/politics/trump-unemployment-numbers-protests/index.html) \(June 2020\).
1.4.1.5.8. Con: [President Trump's trade policies further undermined the confidence](https://finance.yahoo.com/news/dollars-status-worlds-funding-currency-question-144437776.html) and trust global markets had for decades in utilizing the U.S. dollar as a standard currency.
1.4.1.5.8.1. Pro: President Trump had a [17th-century](https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/trumps-trade-policy-is-stuck-in-the-80s--the-1680s/2018/05/31/f8e2f7c2-6510-11e8-a69c-b944de66d9e7_story.html?utm_term=.fbfab00f21c7) [zero-sum view](https://www.wsj.com/articles/the-zero-sum-worlds-of-trump-and-sanders-1458504854) of international trade which was [refuted](http://theconversation.com/trumps-exports-good-imports-bad-trade-policy-debunked-by-an-economist-94625) by [economists](https://qz.com/894085/donald-trumps-mercantilist-trade-policy-was-debunked-by-economist-adam-smith-more-than-200-years-ago/) of all stripes.

Pro: He supports anti-trade policies such as [tariffs](https://taxfoundation.org/tariffs-trump-trade-war/) and has opposed free trade deals such as the [TPP](https://www.google.com/url?sa=t&rct=j&q=&esrc=s&source=web&cd=1&ved=2ahUKEwjqiuOKwMPpAhUWa80KHfVcD3MQFjAAegQICBAB&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.politico.com%2Fstory%2F2019%2F01%2F23%2Ftrans-pacific-trade-pact-2017-1116638&usg=AOvVaw20md5kqynYQV0bQ6N_08pF) and NAFTA while failing to recognize the zero-sum nature of them.

Con: President Trump’s [words](https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/trump-peacefully-and-patriotically/)(After this, we’re going to walk down — and I’ll be there with you — we’re going to walk down, we’re going to walk down — anyone you want, but I think right here — we’re going to walk down to the Capitol, and we’re going to cheer on our brave senators and congressmen and women. And we’re probably not going to be cheering so much for some of them. Because you’ll never take back our country with weakness, you have to show strength, and you have to be strong. The Lee call was one of an unknown number that Trump made during a mysterious gap of 7 hours 37 minutes that exists in the call logs – precisely the timeframe of the Capitol attack.\n\nThose missing call logs, disclosed by the Washington Post and CBS News, raise several burning questions – how did the records disappear? who carried out the excising? – but none more urgent than this: what was Trump trying to hide?\n\n“A gap like this doesn’t happen by accident. It’s not a coincidence,” said Charlie Sykes, columnist at the Trump-resistant conservative outlet the Bulwark. “There is no innocent explanation here – somebody made the decision to rip up the record for the crucial hours of January 6 and there has to be a reason why.”) related to the attack on the Capitol, strongly implying he has something to hide.

1.4.4.2.4.2.1. Con: [Bronchoalveolar lavage \(BAL\)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronchoalveolar_lavage) \(also known as lung washing\) is a diagnostic method of the lower respiratory system in which a [bronchoscope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronchoscope) is passed through the mouth or nose into the [lungs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lung). It has even been used therapeutically to remove mucus, improve airway ventilation, and reduce airway inflammation in conditions such as COPD and PAP. Therefore, suggesting that doctors try injecting fluids into the lungs for cleaning wasn't a completely ridiculous idea.

Pro: James Mattis was opposed to the creation of the Space Force because it would divide "[warfighting functions](https://jscholarship.library.jhu.edu/bitstream/handle/1774.2/61800/Barrow%2C%20Gregory%20D..pdf?sequence=1&isAllowed=y)("\[at\] a time when we are trying to integrate the \[DoD’s\] joint warfighting functions, I do not wish to add a separate service that would likely present a narrower and even parochial approach to space operations.")".

1.4.5.6.2.2. Con: Even James Mattis warned against the creation of the Space Force due to budgetary concerns, he later [supported it](https://thehill.com/policy/defense/400781-mattis-pentagon-white-house-in-complete-agreement-on-space-force).
1.4.5.6.3. Pro: In December 2019, President Trump signed the 2020 [National Defense Authorization Act](https://www.space.com/trump-creates-space-force-2020-defense-bill.html) which directed the establishment of the [U.S. Space Force](https://www.space.com/42089-space-force.html) as the sixth branch of the armed forces.
1.4.5.6.4. Con: The [Air Force Space Command](https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-space-force-is-dumb-says-nasa-astronaut-2018-6?r=US&IR=T)(But retired NASA astronaut Mark Kelly — a former Navy pilot, combat veteran, four-time space-flyer, and the identical twin brother of the former astronaut Scott Kelly — doesn't support the plan, and some members of Congress have also voiced their distaste for the idea.\n\n"This is a dumb idea. The Air Force does this already. That is their job," Mark Kelly tweeted in June, following Trump's remarks. "What's next, we move submarines to the 7th branch and call it the 'under-the-sea force?'"\n\n\[...\]\n\nKelly was referring to the Air Force Space Command, though the group has had different names over the years.\n\nSpace Command is headquartered in Colorado, and its responsibilities include supporting military use of satellites, rocket launches, and cyberwarfare operations. The group also helps track the countless pieces of space junk and debris around Earth that pose a persistent threat to anything in orbit.) already existed when President Trump proposed the Space Force.
1.4.5.7. Pro: The US military had more accomplishments under President Trump's administration than in previous ones.
1.4.5.7.1. Pro: A notable victory for the military under President Trump was defeating ISIS's caliphate and [killing Abu Bakr al-Baghdadi](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-50200339) in 2019.
1.4.5.7.2. Pro: President Trump managed to get other [NATO](https://www.militarytimes.com/news/pentagon-congress/2018/01/19/trumps-biggest-military-accomplishments-as-president-so-far-according-to-the-gop/) member countries to commit to increasing their financial contribution to the military alliance, as [promised](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/promises/trumpometer/promise/1386/ask-countries-we-protect-pay-more-for-joint-defens/).
1.4.5.7.3. Con: President Obama eliminated the leader of al Qaeda, Osama bin Laden, who was responsible for the [9/11 terrorist attacks](https://www.thebalance.com/how-the-9-11-attacks-still-affect-the-economy-today-3305536).
1.4.5.7.4. Con: President Obama repealed the "[Don't ask, don't tell](https://obamawhitehouse.archives.gov/blog/2012/09/20/archives-end-dont-ask-dont-tell)(In 2011, “Don’t Ask, Don’t Tell” was finally and formally repealed, allowing gay and lesbian service members to serve openly in our nation’s armed forces.)" policy in 2011.
1.4.5.8. Con: The military was already far stronger than necessary. It was just a waste of money.
1.4.5.8.1. Pro: Exponentially expanding the military reach and expanding an army's operations are historically unbecoming of great empires, such as Rome. [Researchers believe the U.S. is heading in a similar direction.](https://www.rand.org/pubs/monographs/MG362.html)
1.4.5.8.2. Pro: As of May 2020, the US military spent [more than the next 10 nations combined](https://www.pgpf.org/chart-archive/0053_defense-comparison), of which some are allies or close NATO member-states.
1.4.5.9. Con: President Trump's undermining of the [Uniform Code of Military Justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uniform_Code_of_Military_Justice) \(UCMJ\) with his [pardons of US war criminals](https://www.aa.com.tr/en/americas/us-continues-to-pardon-war-criminals-in-iraq-afghanistan/2088191) were a detriment to morale and order.
1.4.5.10. Pro: Service-members had a more favorable view of President Trump, which will likely improve their morale and service.
1.4.5.10.1. Pro: Only [40%](https://www.militarytimes.com/news/pentagon-congress/2017/10/23/military-times-poll-what-you-really-think-about-trump/) of service-members had a negative view of the President.
1.4.5.10.1.1. Con: Considering how unpopular President Trump was with the public, this statistic doesn't say much. The survey also shows that the majority of officers disapproved of President Trump, with only 30% supporting him.
1.4.5.10.1.1.1. Pro: The only branch of the army where President Trump enjoyed a favorability of over 50% was the Marines, and that was because the Marines loved [Mattis](https://www.marinecorpstimes.com/news/your-marine-corps/2018/10/22/trump-saint-mattis-and-war-marines-are-still-big-fans-even-as-the-other-branches-wane/), President Trump's cabinet pick.
1.4.5.10.1.2. Con: This has changed. 50% of servicemembers had a negative view as of [December 2019](https://www.militarytimes.com/news/pentagon-congress/2019/12/17/half-of-active-duty-service-members-are-unhappy-with-trump-new-military-times-poll-shows/), and it's [likely slipped further](https://www.nytimes.com/2020/06/12/us/politics/trump-polls-military-approval.html) after he announced intentions to use the military against BLM protesters, and other actions.
1.4.5.10.1.3. Con: 40% is a substantial amount of the American population.
1.4.5.10.2. Con: Many veterans were [horrified](https://www.huffpost.com/entry/amvets-trump-mccain-death_n_5b840313e4b03485860253fd) by President Trump's actions towards Sen. John McCain, to the point of the unprecedented step of drafting and sending a letter demanding that he follow protocol.
1.4.5.10.2.1. Pro: President Trump had a long history of [disparaging the military service](https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-under-fire-for-alleged-comments-about-veterans-has-a-long-history-of-disparaging-military-service/2020/09/06/76aba4b8-f053-11ea-9279-45d6bdfe145f_story.html), even though he claimed he had done [more for veterans than John McCain](https://edition.cnn.com/2020/09/04/politics/fact-check-trump-mccain-loser-veterans-choice/index.html) did.
1.4.5.10.3. Con: Given the [increase in defence spending under Trump](https://www.bbc.com/news/election-us-2020-54060026), servicemen were unlikely to be objective in their view.
1.4.5.10.3.1. Pro: In 2018, President Trump requested Congress for [$639 billion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_budget_of_the_United_States) in military spending, which represented a 10% increase since 2017.
1.4.5.10.4. Con: This didn't necessarily mean that President Trump's military policies were sound. Service members' higher rates of support would also be the case if service members were more likely to be Republican in the first place.
1.5. Con: President Trump had low [public](https://news.gallup.com/poll/328637/last-trump-job-approval-average-record-low.aspx)(WASHINGTON, D.C. -- As President Donald Trump prepares to leave the White House, 34% of Americans approve of the job he is doing as president, the worst evaluation of his presidency. His 41% average approval rating throughout his presidency is four points lower than for any of his predecessors in Gallup's polling era. Trump's ratings showed a record 81-percentage-point average gap between Republicans and Democrats -- 11 points wider than the prior record.) and [expert](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2018/02/19/opinion/how-does-trump-stack-up-against-the-best-and-worst-presidents.html) approval.
1.5.1. Con: It is not uncommon for presidents who end up being popular to go through periods of unpopularity and polarisation.
1.5.1.1. Pro: President Trump's approval rating after the first 486 days of his presidency was [the same as Reagan's](https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/trump-approval-ratings/?ex_cid=rrpromo) and Carter's.
1.5.1.2. Pro: Abraham Lincoln was deeply [unpopular](https://www.battlefields.org/learn/articles/evidence-unpopular-mr-lincoln)(At the time he was sworn in, Lincoln's "approval rating" can be estimated by examining wintertime Republican losses in local elections in Brooklyn, Cincinnati, Cleveland and St. Louis, and state elections in Connecticut, Massachusetts and Rhode Island; by the observations of Henry Adams \(of the presidential Adamses\) that "not a third of the House" supported him; and by the published reckoning of the New York Herald that only 1 million of the 4.7 million who voted in November were still with him. All these indications put his support in the nation at about 25 percent — roughly equivalent to the lowest approval ratings recorded by modern-day polling.) for much of his life. He is now routinely ranked as [the greatest president of all time](https://www.smithsonianmag.com/smart-news/who-was-worst-president-everand-how-do-historians-decide-180978105/)(By comparison, Buchanan’s successor, Abraham Lincoln, maintained his tight grip on the top spot for leading the nation through the Civil War and abolishing slavery. He’s the standalone figure in a string of worst-ranked presidents that stretches from 1837 to 1869, notes the Post.\n\nIn general, time tends to be on the side of presidents like Ronald Reagan and Dwight Eisenhower, who were unpopular with historians at the time of leaving office but are highly ranked on 2021’s survey, as participant and Lyndon Johnson historian Mark K. Updegrove points out in a New York Times op-ed. With regards to recent presidents, George W. Bush debuted at 36th place in 2009 but jumped 7 places this year to spot 29; and Barack Obama rose two spots to break into the top 10 presidents this year.).
1.5.1.3. Con: The major difference was the starting approval. [President Trump's approval started under 50%](https://fivethirtyeight.com/features/trump-is-the-most-unpopular-president-since-ford-to-run-for-reelection/) \(with 42.6\) and he ended his presidency with [58% of disapproval](https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/trump-approval-ratings/?ex_cid=rrpromo).
1.5.2. Pro: A [survey of 391 political experts](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2018/02/19/opinion/how-does-trump-stack-up-against-the-best-and-worst-presidents.html) from the [American Political Science Association](https://www.apsanet.org/ABOUT/About-APSA)(Founded in 1903, the American Political Science Association \(APSA\) is the leading professional organization for the study of political science and serves more than 11,000 members in more than 100 countries. With a range of programs and services for individuals, departments, and institutions, APSA brings together political scientists from all fields of inquiry, regions, and occupational endeavors within and outside academe to deepen our understanding of politics, democracy, and citizenship throughout the world. The Association promotes a lively, diverse community of scholars, teachers, students, and practitioners who bring wide-ranging interests, methodologies, and perspectives to the analysis and conduct of government and politics.) ranked him as the worst President.
1.5.2.1. Con: He was much better than the alternative of [Hilary Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton), and so could be comparatively considered, a good President.
1.5.2.1.1. Con: This is all speculative. We can't know how Clinton would have performed given that she [was never elected President](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2017/nov/07/the-night-they-cant-forget-hillary-clinton-supporters-recall-the-election).
1.5.2.1.1.1. Pro: A better comparison would be to [past,](https://www.businessinsider.com/greatest-us-presidents-ranked-by-political-scientists-2018-2#40-andrew-johnson-5) or best [historic](https://www.businessinsider.com/the-top-20-presidents-in-us-history-according-to-historians-2017-2#10-lyndon-b-johnson-11) [presidents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_rankings_of_presidents_of_the_United_States) in US history.
1.5.2.1.1.1.1. Pro: In a comparison against past presidents, President Trump has ranked as "[last in 'Presidential Greatness](https://time.com/5165686/donald-trump-last-place-presidential-greatness/)'.
1.5.2.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: The [top 5 best presidents in US history](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2018/02/19/opinion/how-does-trump-stack-up-against-the-best-and-worst-presidents.html) are considered to be: Lincoln, Washington, F.D. Roosevelt, T. Roosevelt, and Jefferson.
1.5.2.1.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: The [top 5 worst presidents in US history](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2018/02/19/opinion/how-does-trump-stack-up-against-the-best-and-worst-presidents.html) are considered to be: \(from worst to "best"\): Trump, Buchanan, Harding, W.H.Harrison, A. Johnson and Pierce.
1.5.2.1.1.1.1.1.2. Con: [US society has become more diverse](https://www.washingtonpost.com/graphics/national/how-diverse-is-america/) with time, and it is very hard for a single person to "[represent the varied, competing interests of 327 million citizens.](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2018/05/a-broken-office/556883/)(No one man—or woman—can possibly represent the varied, competing interests of 327 million citizens.)"
1.5.2.1.1.1.1.2. Con: In comparison to past Presidents, there has never been more [political polarization than during Trump's presidency](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/fixgov/2018/03/20/comparing-trump-to-the-greatest-and-the-most-polarizing-presidents-in-u-s-history/).
1.5.2.1.1.1.1.2.1. Con: The US has gone through a [Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War) in the past, implying that polarization has had historically worse highs.
1.5.2.1.1.1.1.3. Con: 'Presidential Greatness' is not a meaningfully measurable or objective ranking that gives us any insight into President Trump.
1.5.2.1.1.1.2. Con: The political, economic, and social contexts of US history have evolved with time, therefore [comparing presidents wouldn't be accurate](https://www.brookings.edu/blog/fixgov/2018/03/20/comparing-trump-to-the-greatest-and-the-most-polarizing-presidents-in-u-s-history/).
1.5.2.1.1.2. Con: According to some experts, "[Clinton would not have been able to do much even with the large powers of the presidency.](https://www.econlib.org/counterfactuals-what-if-clinton-had-won-in-2016/)"
1.5.2.1.2. Con: Being better than alternatives did not make President Trump a "good President".
1.5.2.1.2.1. Con: If good is the thing which produces the best outcomes in a given scenario, than being better than the only alternative would make the object good.
1.5.2.1.3. Pro: Hillary Clinton would have been a worse President than Donald Trump.
1.5.2.1.3.1. Pro: Hillary's campaign conspired with foreign intelligence operatives and [top Justice Department officials](https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/news/bruce-ohr-bypassed-doj-superiors-to-feed-fbi-info-from-trump-dossier-author-report) to undermine the election by funding an [unverifiable propaganda document](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump–Russia_dossier) for the purpose of undermining a presidential nominee. The conceit this shows indicates Hillary would have been a worse President.
1.5.2.1.3.1.1. Con: Unverifiable in places, but [never disproved](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump%E2%80%93Russia_dossier). Indeed, more and more has been proven true over time, and the intelligence community has been and is investigating the allegations.
1.5.2.1.3.1.2. Con: It is perfectly common practise to engage in smear campaigns during Presidential elections; Trump did precisely the same thing in reverse with his nickname "[Crooked Hillary](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2017/07/whats-wrong-with-the-democrats/528696/)".
1.5.2.1.3.1.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.5.1.2.
1.5.2.1.3.1.3. Con: Given the level of President [Trump's own arrogance](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/people/donald-trump-president-wins-us-election-2016-who-is-he-life-career-quotes-hillary-clinton-a7402211.html), this is not the best line of argument. Regardless of how valid or invalid Hillary's actions were, to criticise her conceit in comparison to President Trump is challenging.
1.5.2.1.3.1.4. Con: The initial research that preceded and, speculatively, may have later led to the Steele Dossier was actually commissioned by Republicans and later picked up by the Democrats, as the [timeline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump%E2%80%93Russia_dossier) of Republican and Democrat funding for Fusion GPS indicates.
1.5.2.1.3.1.4.1. Con: Christopher Steele was not [hired or commissioned to work](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump%E2%80%93Russia_dossier) on the Steele Dossier until after the Republicans had ceased funding. As such, it is unclear how much of the initial research from their funding went into it or even would have led to it.
1.5.2.1.3.1.4.1.1. Con: At what point Fusion GPS decided to contract Steele is unclear. It may have been when they were still on the Republican payroll, though it is an undisputed fact that his research did not begin until after the Republicans ceased payment.
1.5.2.1.3.1.4.1.1.1. Con: However, under the assumption that when Republican funding ceased, it meant that whatever [Fusion GPS were doing](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/10/27/us/politics/trump-dossier-paul-singer.html) for the Republicans also stopped, it can be said almost conclusively that the Republicans didn't fund the Steele dossier.
1.5.2.1.3.1.4.2. Con: This speculation is inconsistent with what the republican group, Free Beacon, has said. [Namely:](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trump–Russia_dossier)"All of the work that Fusion GPS provided to the Free Beacon was based on public sources, and none of the work product that the Free Beacon received appears in the Steele dossier. The Free Beacon had no knowledge of or connection to the Steele dossier, did not pay for the dossier, and never had contact with, knowledge of, or provided payment for any work performed by Christopher Steele."
1.5.2.1.3.2. Pro: Hillary ran on a platform of [continuation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton_2016_presidential_campaign) of Obama's presidency. Therefore it was reasonable to consider that the unexpected economic and jobs boom attributable to President Trump's policy changes on tax and regulations would not have happened had Hillary been president.

Therefore it was reasonable to consider that the improved dialogue and behaviour of North Korea would not have happened had Hillary been elected.

1.5.2.2. Pro: According to some [historians](https://www.smh.com.au/world/north-america/is-donald-trump-the-worst-us-president-ever-historians-say-so-20210115-p56u9w.html), President Trump was the worst President in US history.
1.5.2.3. Pro: When asked, even [conservative scholars](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-46895634)(Though the president has likened himself to Abraham Lincoln, who posterity has deemed to be greatest of all presidents, this survey judged him to be the worst of the worst. 1.5.2.4. Con: In 2014 Obama was rated by 33% of participants in a poll as the [worst president since World War II.](https://www.usatoday.com/story/theoval/2014/07/02/obama-george-w-bush-quinnipiac-poll-reagan-clinton/11985837/)
1.5.2.4.1. Con: These numbers don't imply a genuine negative consensus, as 67% of respondents didn't believe Obama was the worst president since World War II.
1.5.2.4.1.1. Con: A genuine negative consensus is precisely what you would expect from biased people expressing cognitive dissonance.
1.5.2.4.1.1.1. Con: The referenced poll includes Democrat, Independent, and Republican scholars. In all groups, President Trump was rated in the bottom five, indicating that political bias was less of a factor in the results.

In 2018 the [same group repeated it](https://eu.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/onpolitics/2018/03/07/quinnipiac-poll-41-say-trump-worst-president-since-world-war-ii/404118002/) and President Trump was at the top with 41% as compared to President Obama at 21%.

Con: The poll cited regarding Obama was not by political experts in any way or form; those with [qualifications from APSA](https://poll.qu.edu/national/release-detail?ReleaseID=2056)(The American Political Science Association \(APSA\).) are considerably more valid than popularity contests.
