1.5.3. Pro: -> See 1.4.4.3.
1.5.4. Pro: President Trump seemed untrustworthy because he didn't seem to know what he was talking about at any given time.

1.5.4.1.1. Pro: President Trump's quotes on [mental health](https://www.huffingtonpost.co.uk/entry/donald-trump-mental-illness_n_57583b02e4b0ced23ca691b5?guccounter=1) demonstrated no understanding of the issue, folding both to stigma and misinformation.

1.5.4.1.1.1.1. Pro: There's a link between illness and crime. [One-third of mass shootings are committed by people with mental illness](https://www.pewtrusts.org/en/research-and-analysis/blogs/stateline/2019/08/08/one-third-of-mass-shootings-committed-by-people-with-mental-illness-study-says).

And they're going to do things that people will not even believe are possible." - this was an example of President Trump's gross misrepresentation of people with mental health problems. \([Meet the Press, 4/10/15](https://www.shortlist.com/news/most-ridiculous-trump-quotes-ever/54443)\)

1.5.4.2.6.1.1. Pro: It has been shown that undocumented immigrants are actually half as likely to [be arrested for violent crimes as U.S.-born citizens](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/undocumented-immigrants-are-half-as-likely-to-be-arrested-for-violent-crimes-as-u-s-born-citizens/).

1.5.4.2.6.1.2.2. Pro: Illegally entering a country can be both convicted as a crime and held responsible for a civil violation under the [U.S. immigration laws](https://www.alllaw.com/articles/nolo/us-immigration/crime-enter-illegally.html).

1.5.4.2.6.2.1.3. Pro: In light of the protests and counter-protests in [Charlottesville](https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2017/08/trump-defends-white-nationalist-protesters-some-very-fine-people-on-both-sides/537012/), he tarred both sides with the same brush, equating the protesters of ANTIFA on the left, with [White Supremacists and Neo-Nazis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unite_the_Right_rally) on the right. This drew a lot of criticism of President Trump.
1.5.4.2.6.2.1.3.1. Pro: The rally was organised by [Richard Spencer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_B._Spencer), a white supremacist. The rally was white supremacist, antisemitic, white separatist, and neo-fascist.
1.5.4.2.6.2.1.3.1.1. Pro: President Trump later amended his statement to say that there were "[some fine, very fine people, on both sides](https://www.politifact.com/article/2019/apr/26/context-trumps-very-fine-people-both-sides-remarks/)", again a sweeping generalisation.

Pro: Although there were undoubtedly some innocent and/or peaceful protesters on the right, many of the marchers [chanted racist and antisemitic slogans](https://indianexpress.com/article/world/charlottesville-violence-from-nazi-slogans-to-counter-protests-heres-what-happened-in-the-virginia-city-4794475/), carried semi-automatic rifles, swastikas, Nazi symbols etc. Because of this, many feel he has said there are "very fine" Neo-Nazis/Nazi sympathisers.

1.5.4.2.6.2.2.1. Pro: In 2019, [43% of the 11.6 million immigrants from Mexico](https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2019/06/28/what-we-know-about-illegal-immigration-from-mexico/) living in the United States were in the country illegally.

1.5.4.5. Pro: President Trump had [no understanding of climate change](https://friendsoftheearth.uk/climate-change/donald-trump-stupid-quotes).

1.5.4.5.4. Pro: President Trump attempted to argue that global warming was a [Chinese hoax](https://www.forbes.com/sites/davidvolodzko/2019/02/23/manufacturing-climate-denial-is-a-threat-to-manufacturing/#3e19c9ad21b9)(The concept of global warming was created by and for the Chinese in order to make U.S. manufacturing non-competitive.\n\n — Donald J. Trump \(\@realDonaldTrump\) November 6, 2012).
1.5.4.5.4.1. Pro: President Trump derided [climate change](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-37982000) as a hoax concocted by China and the regulations of Paris as stifling to American growth.
1.5.4.5.4.1.1. Pro: As a consequence of President Trump's views on the regulations of Paris, the U.S withdrew from the [Paris agreement on the 1st of June 2017](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_withdrawal_from_the_Paris_Agreement).

1.5.4.5.4.2. Con: In 2009, Trump signed [a full-page advert in the New York Times](https://grist.org/politics/donald-trump-climate-action-new-york-times/), expressing his support for legislation [combating climate change](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-51213003).
1.5.4.5.5. Pro: President Trump denied that climate change is a lasting problem and believed it will "[fix itself](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2018/oct/15/itll-change-back-trump-says-climate-change-not-a-hoax-but-denies-lasting-impact)", countering science and blaming scientists for having their own "[agenda](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-45859325)".

Con: President Trump publicly acknowledged the [role of humans in climate change](https://apnews.com/article/election-2020-joe-biden-donald-trump-technology-politics-b5ae9468286d92f44c6a10d1e6d2cad0)(Trump said \[...\] that humans — their tailpipe exhaust, oil and gas production, and smokestack fumes — are just one of many culprits for the weather-disrupting deterioration of Earth’s atmosphere.).
1.5.4.6. Pro: President Trump had a [flawed](https://www.theatlantic.com/ideas/archive/2018/07/why-donald-trumps-trade-war-will-fail/564605/) [understanding](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/trump-trade-war_us_5ac53929e4b09ef3b2432f64) of [economics](https://www.vanityfair.com/news/2018/07/donald-trump-seems-confused-about-whos-paying-for-his-trade-war) and international politics.
1.5.4.6.1. Pro: President Trump thought that trade wars were [good things](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2018-03-01/trump-is-said-to-delay-decision-on-steel-and-aluminum-tariffs) and [easy to win](http://www.latimes.com/world/asia/la-fg-china-trade-fight-20180625-story.html).
1.5.4.6.2. Con: Some of [President Trump's formulas for growing the U.S. economy](https://www.brookings.edu/research/trumps-formula-for-growing-the-u-s-economy-what-will-work-and-what-wont/) worked, which showed his understanding of economics.
1.5.4.6.3. Con: President Trump’s position towards [Brexit and towards the European Union showed opportunism](https://journals.openedition.org/lisa/10235?lang=en), which was a sign that he understood foreign affairs and international politics.
1.5.4.6.3.1. Pro: President Trump had a clear [foreign policy ideology](https://ecpr.eu/Events/Event/PaperDetails/35011) which, like all American presidents, drew on nationalism and opportunism.

1.5.5. Con: It is impossible to judge the public approval of President Trump by media charts and ‘expert’ panels.
1.5.5.1. Pro: [Before the 2016 election](https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/11/09/why-2016-election-polls-missed-their-mark/), the media made it look as though Trump had little public popularity when compared with Clinton. This was proven false by the voter outcome.
1.5.5.2. Con: The 2020 election was the largest possible poll of approval and in that election Trump lost by a significant margin, becoming one of only [10 US presidents in history to fail to get reelected](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-politics/how-many-us-presidents-lost-second-term-b1640998.html).
1.5.5.2.1. Con: Even though he lost the 2020 presidential election, Donald Trump still earned the [second-highest number of votes](https://www.cfr.org/blog/2020-election-numbers)(Biden won 81,283,098 votes, or 51.3 percent of the votes cast. He is the first U.S. presidential candidate to have won more than 80 million votes. Trump won 74,222,958 votes, or 46.8 percent of the votes cast. That’s more votes than any other presidential candidate has ever won, with the exception of Biden. \(Third-party candidates picked up 1.8 percent of the votes cast.\)) of any presidential candidate in history.
1.5.6. Pro: He did not get the [majority of votes](https://www.pewresearch.org/politics/2018/08/09/an-examination-of-the-2016-electorate-based-on-validated-voters/). He won because of the [voting system in the US](https://www.usa.gov/election).
1.5.6.1. Con: This doesn't mean that he had low approval ratings, this means that he had enough approval to trigger the [exception of the voting system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College).
1.5.6.2. Con: Other candidates have won the presidency [without a majority of votes](https://time.com/5579161/presidents-elected-electoral-college/)(No matter whether the Electoral College changes or stays in place, however, the Electoral College has already left an indelible mark on some of the most consequential moments in American history, determining who was in power during the Sept. 11 attacks and the Reconstruction period after the Civil War.\n\nHere’s a full list of Presidents elected by the Electoral College without winning the popular vote.).
1.5.6.3. Pro: Hillary Clinton received [nearly three million more votes](https://www.nytimes.com/elections/2016/results/president) than Donald Trump in the 2016 election.
1.5.7. Con: This is an appeal to popularity or "[argumentum ad populum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Argumentum_ad_populum)(An argumentum ad populum \(Latin for "appeal to the people"\) is a fallacious argument that concludes that a proposition must be true because many or most people believe it, often concisely encapsulated as: "If many believe so, it is so".)" \(appeal to the people\) which is a common logical fallacy.
1.5.7.1. Con: Effectiveness in terms of a democratically elected head of state can only be measured in the [representativeness of the public will](https://www.annualreviews.org/doi/pdf/10.1146/annurev.polisci.11.053006.190533)(The topic of political representation hasbecome increasingly visible and importantwithin contemporary democratic theory fortwo reasons. The first is a disjunction betweenthe standard accounts of democratic repre-sentation, focused primarily on territoriallybased electoral representation, and an increas-ingly complex political terrain, which is lessconfined within state territoriality, more plu-ralized, and increasingly dependent on infor-mal negotiation and deliberation to generatepolitical legitimacy.). \(p. 388\)
1.5.7.1.1. Con: Political polarization has increased "[partisan motivated reasoning](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s11109-019-09539-8)(Due to changes in the US political environment in the last few decades, we suspect that the relative importance of these components has changed over time. In particular, we argue that polarization has increased partisan motivated reasoning when it comes to evaluations of the president.)" regarding any president's evaluations.
1.5.7.2. Pro: [People are influenced by the media](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/pdf/10.1111/spsr.12263)(Due to their role as intermediaries between the political system and the public, mediaorganizations and journalists who produce and relay content to citizens play a major rolein current democracies.), therefore public and expert approval can be manipulated. \(p. 1\)
1.5.7.2.1. Con: People are influenced by the media, however certains groups within the media overdefend Trump, which might have actually increased his popularity above what it would be in a more objective setting.
1.5.7.2.1.1. Pro: Media outlets, such as [Fox News](https://www.nytimes.com/2021/05/28/business/media/trump-fox-news.html), put out extremely positive material on Trump.
1.5.7.2.1.2. Pro: Trump was a master of mobilising the power of [ressentiment \(p. 81\)](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/321225465_Trump_Propaganda_and_the_Politics_of_Ressentiment) and applying it through mass and social media.
1.5.7.2.1.3. Pro: One America News Network has been accused of peddling pro-Trump propaganda to such a degree that [they are being threatened with legal action for defamation](https://www.vanityfair.com/news/2021/04/trumps-biggest-propaganda-machine-doesnt-believe-its-own-lies).
1.5.7.2.1.4. Pro: With a final approval rating of just [34%](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_presidential_approval_rating#President_Donald_Trump), it is possible for a significant proportion of Trump's remaining support to come from media propaganda.
1.5.7.3. Con: However, [public](https://www.britannica.com/topic/public-opinion) [opinion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_opinion) and [approval](https://saylordotorg.github.io/text_american-government-and-politics-in-the-information-age/s11-01-what-is-public-opinion.html), as well as [public](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opinion_poll#:~:text=Opinion%20polls%20are%20usually%20designed,referred%20to%20as%20a%20pollster.) [opinion polls](https://www.britannica.com/topic/public-opinion/Public-opinion-and-government), are [good](https://www.historians.org/about-aha-and-membership/aha-history-and-archives/gi-roundtable-series/pamphlets/em-4-are-opinion-polls-useful-\(1946\)/is-it-important-to-know-public-opinion) [metrics](https://www.ipsos.com/ipsos-mori/en-uk/public-opinion-why-it-important-and-how-measure-it) as to whether someone is doing a good job and is, [subjectively](https://www.brookings.edu/articles/polling-public-opinion-the-good-the-bad-and-the-ugly/), a "good" President.
1.5.7.3.1. Pro: Most democracies use public opinion polls, as well as popular vote for candidates in elections. This would represent public opinion and is the corner stone of a [democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy#:~:text=Democracy%20\(Greek%3A%20%CE%B4%CE%B7%CE%BC%CE%BF%CE%BA%CF%81%CE%B1%CF%84%CE%AF%CE%B1%2C%20d%C4%93mokrati%C4%81,to%20choose%20their%20governing%20legislators.).
1.5.7.3.2. Pro: Most respected and reputable opinion polls are conducted at random to try to get a representative sample and eliminate bias, thus giving a good indication of general public consensus and feeling.
1.5.7.3.2.1. Con: Many polls may be subject to [reporting bias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reporting_bias) and [non-response bias](https://delighted.com/blog/avoid-7-types-sampling-response-survey-bias), where only people motivated to answer do so, creating a skew in the results.
1.5.7.3.2.1.1. Pro: This was particularly evident in exit polls for both the 2016 and 2020 elections, where the media and pollsters regularly got it wrong and did not expect such tight or close races.
1.5.7.3.2.1.2. Pro: Many Republican \(and Trump\) supporters allegedly gave [false or misleading](https://www.cloudresearch.com/resources/blog/election-2020-poll-respondent-honesty/) answers, because they distrusted the pollsters and media.
1.5.7.3.2.2. Pro: Trump consistently [polled badly overall in a majority of polls](https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/trump-approval-ratings/), and left office with the [lowest first-term approval of any President, ever](https://www.cnn.com/2021/01/16/politics/trump-approval-analysis/index.html), with one of the lowest approval rates and one of the highest disapproval rates.
1.5.7.3.3. Pro: Public opinion and voting are used in popularity contests, pageants, and other forms of public voting. Public opinion is subjective but this is one way to realistically measure it.
1.5.7.3.4. Con: "Good" is subjective. Different people have different definitions of what is "good" compared to others.
1.6. Con: President Trump may not have been [loyal](https://www.irishtimes.com/culture/books/could-donald-trump-really-be-spying-for-vladimir-putin-1.3604145) to the United States.
1.6.1. Con: President Trump tried his best to keep his word for what he promised his electorate.
1.6.1.1. Pro: President Trump tried his best to [build a wall](https://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/opinion/donald-trump-build-wall-191019103020859.html), stand up to [China](https://edition.cnn.com/2019/09/25/perspectives/china-trade-war-trump-winning/index.html), and bring back [jobs](https://www.forbes.com/sites/chuckdevore/2019/03/11/trumps-policy-magic-wand-boosts-manufacturing-jobs-399-in-first-26-months-over-obamas-last-26/#97022fc20a63), whether he succeeded in doing so or not.
1.6.1.1.1. Con: There is not enough evidence that he tried his best. Neither the amount of documentation worked through, nor work hours clocked \(and other Key Performance Indicators\) are available to the public.
1.6.1.1.1.1. Pro: Health stats are commonly available nowadays and this information is not available to the public.
1.6.1.1.2. Con: President Trump didn't care about human rights, as building a wall over the Mexican border would have been similar to the [Berlin Wall](https://www.icj.org/the-berlin-wall-a-defiance-of-human-rights/).

1.6.1.2.7. Con: President Trump promised '[giant tax cuts](https://economictimes.indiatimes.com/news/international/world-news/donald-trump-promises-giant-tax-cut-as-christmas-gift-to-americans/articleshow/62067936.cms?from=mdr)' for the Americans and went through with them.

Con: Trump reneged on a [pledge](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/the-fix/wp/2016/09/26/the-first-trump-clinton-presidential-debate-transcript-annotated/?utm_term=.841a57eff5a2) to release his tax returns after an IRS audit \(despite the fact that [nothing precludes a President from releasing tax returns while under audit](https://www.politifact.com/virginia/statements/2016/oct/05/tim-kaine/tim-kaine-correctly-notes-richard-nixon-released-t/)\), giving [more than a dozen excuses](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/business/wp/2016/09/15/a-running-tally-of-trumps-many-excuses-for-why-he-wont-release-his-tax-returns/?postshare=5411484153288819) with new reasons tacked on after he was elected.
1.6.1.3.5. Pro: President Trump failed many of his promises related to [his immigration plan](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/promises/trumpometer/subjects/immigration/).

Pro: President Trump made no progress towards building a safe zone in Syria for Syrian refugees as proposed in [a town hall debate](https://www.realclearpolitics.com/video/2015/10/26/republican_voter_challenges_trump_explain_how_you_would_you_deport_all_illegal_immigrants.html). His push for an [immediate withdrawal](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/04/04/world/middleeast/trump-syria-troops.html) of troops from the areas also stood at odds with this goal.

Green card refugees from Syria or elsewhere remained lawful permanent residents.

1.6.1.3.6. Con: President Trump delivered to lower the corporate tax rate and bring in huge tax cuts for working Americans when [the Republican tax plan passed in December 2017.](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/12/19/us/politics/tax-bill-vote-congress.html)

1.6.1.3.8. Con: President Trump delivered his promise [cut as many as 70% of US federal regulations if elected](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-37982000)(The president has slashed through regulations on everything from labour to the environment.\n\nJust days after taking office he signed the Presidential Executive Order on Reducing Regulation and Controlling Regulatory Costs, which mandated that when government departments asked for a federal regulation, they had to specify two others they would drop.\n\nThroughout his term he has continued to slash back red tape. In January 2020 he scrapped protections for US wetlands and streams, and in July he announced changes to the National Environmental Protection Act in a bid to speed up infrastructure projects.\n\n"We are reclaiming America's proud heritage as a nation that gets things done," he said.).

Waterboarding remains illegal.

Pro: President Trump has failed to propose any specific action with regards to libel laws, despite promising to do so in a [rally](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vExmqVkv1ds) in Fort Worth, and further suggesting an intention to [on Twitter](https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/847455180912181249).

1.6.1.5. Pro: President Trump promised that he will appoint Supreme Court judges who "[respect the Second Amendment and what it stands for](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-37982000)(I am looking for judges and have actually picked 20 of them. They'll respect the Second Amendment and what it stands for and what it represents.)". This was delivered by appointing [Neil Gorsuch and Brett Kavanaugh](https://www.cnbc.com/2019/06/28/trumps-two-supreme-court-justices-kavanaugh-and-gorsuch-diverge.html) to these positions.

1.6.1.6. Con: President Trump [broke more promises than he kept](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/promises/trumpometer/?ruling=true).
1.6.1.6.1. Pro: None of the healthcare plans that President Trump promised were delivered.
1.6.1.6.1.1. Pro: Despite promising not to, the Trump administration made [significant cuts](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2019/3/12/18260271/trump-medicaid-social-security-medicare-budget-cuts) to Social Security and Medicaid.
1.6.1.6.1.2. Pro: Despite [promising to do so](https://web.archive.org/web/20161110004206/https://www.donaldjtrump.com/positions/healthcare-reform), President Trump failed to add any price transparency provisions to the House GOP bill, nor implement any changes requiring price transparency from health care providers.
1.6.1.6.1.3. Pro: President Trump failed to allow individuals to deduct health care insurance premiums from taxes as promised on his [campaign website](https://web.archive.org/web/20161110004206/https://www.donaldjtrump.com/positions/healthcare-reform).
1.6.1.6.1.4. Pro: President Trump failed to administer Medicaid through block grants as promised in his campaign website's [health care reform page](https://web.archive.org/web/20161110004206/https://www.donaldjtrump.com/positions/healthcare-reform).
1.6.1.6.1.5. Pro: President Trump promised to [repeal Obamacare](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/promises/trumpometer/?ruling=true)(“Real change begins with immediately repealing and replacing the disaster known as Obamacare."), but didn't.
1.6.1.6.1.5.1. Con: President Trump was responsible for [five big changes to Obamacare](https://www.npr.org/sections/health-shots/2019/10/14/768731628/trump-is-trying-hard-to-thwart-obamacare-hows-that-going).
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.1. Pro: The [individual mandate](https://www.npr.org/sections/health-shots/2019/10/14/768731628/trump-is-trying-hard-to-thwart-obamacare-hows-that-going), by which all US residents were required to either have health insurance or pay a penalty, was eliminated by President Trump in 2017.
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.1.1. Con: Even though the $0 penalty didn't actually go into effect until 2019, it caused insurance premiums to [rise 32% on average in 2018](https://www.kff.org/health-costs/issue-brief/how-premiums-are-changing-in-2018/).
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.2. Pro: President Trump allowed states to add "[work requirements" to Medicaid](https://www.kff.org/medicaid/issue-brief/understanding-the-intersection-of-medicaid-and-work-what-does-the-data-say/).
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.2.1. Pro: With this change, states could require Medicaid beneficiaries to [prove with documentation that they either work or go to school.](http://about:blank)
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.2.2. Con: Many [states didn't implement](http://accounts.google.com/) this change by the end of Trump's administration \(January 2021\).
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.3. Pro: President Trump's administration significantly [cut federal funding](https://www.cms.gov/newsroom/press-releases/cms-announcement-aca-navigator-program-and-promotion-upcoming-open-enrollment) for [Navigator programs](https://www.healthcare.gov/glossary/navigator/).
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.3.1. Pro: These programs [facilitated HealthCare.gov sign-ups](https://cdphe.colorado.gov/health-navigator/role) and helped people figure out the specifics of the new federally run insurance exchanges and sign up for coverage.
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.3.2. Con: Because of this change, the rate of uninsured Americans [increased by 7.9% in 2018](https://www.census.gov/library/publications/2019/demo/p60-267.html)("In 2018, 8.5 percent of people, or 27.5 million, did not have health insurance at any point during the year. The uninsured rate and number of uninsured increased from 2017 \(7.9 percent or 25.6 million\).").
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.4. Pro: The limitations on [short-term insurance policies](https://www.federalregister.gov/documents/2018/08/03/2018-16568/short-term-limited-duration-insurance) were expanded by President Trump's administration.
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.4.1. Con: Some [states have passed their own rules](https://www.healthinsurance.org/so-long-to-limits-on-short-term-plans/#statebills) regarding these short-term or "skinny" plans, and they can either limit it or expand it.
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.4.2. Pro: The Trump administration expanded these short-term plans \(also called "skinny plans"\) to last [364 days and to be renewable for three years](https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefings-statements/remarks-president-trump-expanding-health-coverage-options-small-businesses-workers/)("We took swift action to open short-term health plans and association health plans to millions and millions of Americans. Many of these options are already reducing the cost of health insurance premiums by up to 60% and, really, more than that." — President Trump, The White House, June 14, 2019.).
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.5. Pro: [Cost-sharing reduction subsidies](https://www.npr.org/sections/health-shots/2017/10/14/557602613/trump-decision-to-end-insurance-subsidies-sparks-outrage-lawsuits) to insurers ended in 2017.
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.5.1. Con: This change forced insurers to offer subsidies to low-income people applying for insurance, however, [the federal government did not reimburse them anymore](https://www.npr.org/sections/health-shots/2019/10/14/768731628/trump-is-trying-hard-to-thwart-obamacare-hows-that-going).
1.6.1.6.1.5.1.5.2. Pro: According to President Trump, this change was applied because that money was used to [raise insurance companies' stock prices](https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefings-statements/remarks-president-trump-prime-minister-tsipras-greece-joint-press-conference/)("I knocked out the hundreds of millions of dollars a month being paid back to the insurance companies by politicians. ...
